<div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Federal constitutional monarchy in Western Europe</div>

</p>

<p><b>Belgium</b>,<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;A&#93;</a></sup> officially the <b>Kingdom of Belgium</b>, is a <a href="/wiki/Sovereign_state" title="Sovereign state">sovereign state</a> in <a href="/wiki/Western_Europe" title="Western Europe">Western Europe</a>. It is bordered by the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Netherlands</a> to the north, <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a> to the east, <a href="/wiki/Luxembourg" title="Luxembourg">Luxembourg</a> to the southeast, <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a> to the southwest, and the <a href="/wiki/North_Sea" title="North Sea">North Sea</a> to the northwest. It covers an area of 30,688&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (11,849&#160;sq&#160;mi) and has a population of more than 11.4 million. The capital and largest city is <a href="/wiki/Brussels" title="Brussels">Brussels</a>; other major cities are <a href="/wiki/Antwerp" title="Antwerp">Antwerp</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ghent" title="Ghent">Ghent</a>, <a href="/wiki/Charleroi" title="Charleroi">Charleroi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Li%C3%A8ge" title="Liège">Liège</a>.
</p><p>Belgium is a <a href="/wiki/Federation" title="Federation">federal</a> <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_monarchy" title="Constitutional monarchy">constitutional monarchy</a> with a <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_system" title="Parliamentary system">parliamentary system</a>. Its institutional organization is complex and is structured on both regional and linguistic grounds. It is divided into three highly <a href="/wiki/Autonomous" class="mw-redirect" title="Autonomous">autonomous</a> <a href="/wiki/Communities,_regions_and_language_areas_of_Belgium" title="Communities, regions and language areas of Belgium">regions</a>:<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Flemish_Region" title="Flemish Region">Flanders</a> in the north, <a href="/wiki/Wallonia" title="Wallonia">Wallonia</a> in the south, and the <a href="/wiki/Brussels" title="Brussels">Brussels-Capital Region</a>. Brussels is the smallest and most densely populated region, as well as the richest region in terms of <a href="/wiki/GDP_per_capita" class="mw-redirect" title="GDP per capita">GDP per capita</a>.
</p><p>Belgium is home to two main linguistic groups or <i><a href="/wiki/Communities,_regions_and_language_areas_of_Belgium" title="Communities, regions and language areas of Belgium">communities</a></i>: the Dutch-speaking, mostly <a href="/wiki/Flemish_Community" title="Flemish Community">Flemish Community</a>, which constitutes about 59 percent of the population, and the <a href="/wiki/French_Community_of_Belgium" title="French Community of Belgium">French-speaking Community</a>, which comprises about 40 percent of all Belgians. A small <a href="/wiki/German-speaking_Community_of_Belgium" title="German-speaking Community of Belgium">German-speaking Community</a>, numbering around one percent, exists in the <a href="/wiki/East_Cantons" class="mw-redirect" title="East Cantons">East Cantons</a>. The Brussels-Capital Region is officially bilingual (French and Dutch), although French is the dominant language.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> Belgium's linguistic diversity and related political conflicts are reflected in its <a href="/wiki/History_of_Belgium" title="History of Belgium">political history</a> and <a href="/wiki/Communities,_regions_and_language_areas_of_Belgium" title="Communities, regions and language areas of Belgium">complex system of governance</a>, made up of <a href="/wiki/List_of_governments_in_Belgium" title="List of governments in Belgium">six different governments</a>.
</p><p>Historically, Belgium is part of an area known as the <a href="/wiki/Low_Countries" title="Low Countries">Low Countries</a>, a somewhat larger region than the current <a href="/wiki/Benelux" title="Benelux">Benelux</a> group of states that also included parts of northern France and western Germany. Its name is derived from the Latin word '<b>Belgium'</b>, used by <a href="/wiki/Julius_Caesar" title="Julius Caesar">Julius Caesar</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Gallic_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Gallic War">Gallic War</a></i>, which described the region in the period around 55BCE.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> From the end of the <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">Middle Ages</a> until the 17th century, the area of Belgium was a prosperous and cosmopolitan center of commerce and culture. Between the 16th and early 19th centuries, Belgium served as the battleground between many European powers, earning the moniker the "Battlefield of Europe",<sup id="cite_ref-Hass_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hass-12">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> a reputation strengthened by both <a href="/wiki/World_war" title="World war">world wars</a>. The country emerged in 1830 following the <a href="/wiki/Belgian_Revolution" title="Belgian Revolution">Belgian Revolution</a> when it seceded from the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_of_the_Netherlands" title="United Kingdom of the Netherlands">Netherlands</a>.
</p><p>Belgium participated in the <a href="/wiki/Industrial_Revolution" title="Industrial Revolution">Industrial Revolution</a><sup id="cite_ref-Fitzmaurice_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fitzmaurice-13">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-EUbusiness_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EUbusiness-14">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> and, during the course of the 20th century, possessed <a href="/wiki/Belgian_overseas_colonies" class="mw-redirect" title="Belgian overseas colonies">a number of colonies in Africa</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Karl_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Karl-15">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> The second half of the 20th century was marked by rising tensions between the Dutch-speaking and the French-speaking citizens  fueled by <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Belgium" title="Culture of Belgium">differences in language and culture</a> and the <a href="/wiki/North-South_divide_in_Belgium" class="mw-redirect" title="North-South divide in Belgium">unequal economic development</a> of Flanders and Wallonia. This continuing antagonism has led to several <a href="/wiki/State_reform_in_Belgium" title="State reform in Belgium">far-reaching reforms</a>, resulting in a transition from a <a href="/wiki/Unitary_state" title="Unitary state">unitary</a> to a <a href="/wiki/Federalism" title="Federalism">federal</a> arrangement during the period from 1970 to 1993. Despite the reforms, tensions between the groups have remained, if not increased; there is significant separatism particularly <a href="/wiki/Flemish_Movement" title="Flemish Movement">among the Flemish</a>; controversial language laws exist such as the <a href="/wiki/Municipalities_with_language_facilities" title="Municipalities with language facilities">municipalities with language facilities</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-UCL_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UCL-16">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> and the formation of a coalition government took 18 months following the <a href="/wiki/Belgian_federal_election,_2010" class="mw-redirect" title="Belgian federal election, 2010">June 2010 federal election</a>, a world record.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> Unemployment in Wallonia is more than double that of Flanders, which boomed after the war.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Belgium is one of the six founding countries of the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> and its capital, Brussels, hosts the official seats of the <a href="/wiki/European_Commission" title="European Commission">European Commission</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Council_of_the_European_Union" title="Council of the European Union">Council of the European Union</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/European_Council" title="European Council">European Council</a>, as well as one of two seats of the <a href="/wiki/European_Parliament" title="European Parliament">European Parliament</a> (the other being <a href="/wiki/Strasbourg" title="Strasbourg">Strasbourg</a>). Belgium is also a founding member of the <a href="/wiki/Eurozone" title="Eurozone">Eurozone</a>, <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a>, <a href="/wiki/Organisation_for_Economic_Co-operation_and_Development" class="mw-redirect" title="Organisation for Economic Co-operation and Development">OECD</a>, and <a href="/wiki/World_Trade_Organization" title="World Trade Organization">WTO</a>, and a part of the trilateral Benelux Union and the <a href="/wiki/Schengen_Area" title="Schengen Area">Schengen Area</a>. Brussels hosts several of the EU's official seats as well as the headquarters of many major international organizations such as NATO.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;B&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Belgium is a <a href="/wiki/Developed_country" title="Developed country">developed country</a>, with an advanced <a href="/wiki/World_Bank_high-income_economy" title="World Bank high-income economy">high-income economy</a>. It has very high standards of <a href="/wiki/Standard_of_living" title="Standard of living">living</a>, <a href="/wiki/Quality_of_life" title="Quality of life">quality of life</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Health_care" title="Health care">healthcare</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Education" title="Education">education</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> and is categorized as "very high" in the <a href="/wiki/Human_Development_Index" title="Human Development Index">Human Development Index</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> It also ranks as one of the <a href="/wiki/Global_Peace_Index" title="Global Peace Index">safest or most peaceful countries</a> in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

</div>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Belgium" title="History of Belgium">History of Belgium</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pre-independent_Belgium">Pre-independent Belgium</span></h3>
<div class="quotebox pullquote floatleft" style="width:33%;&#32;;"><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r887775652">.mw-parser-output .quotebox{background-color:#F9F9F9;border:1px solid #aaa;box-sizing:border-box;padding:10px;font-size:88%;max-width:100%}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatleft{margin:0.5em 1.4em 0.8em 0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatright{margin:0.5em 0 0.8em 1.4em}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.centered{margin:0.5em auto 0.8em auto}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatleft p,.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatright p{font-style:inherit}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-title{background-color:#F9F9F9;text-align:center;font-size:larger;font-weight:bold}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-quote.quoted:before{font-family:"Times New Roman",serif;font-weight:bold;font-size:large;color:gray;content:" “ ";vertical-align:-45%;line-height:0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-quote.quoted:after{font-family:"Times New Roman",serif;font-weight:bold;font-size:large;color:gray;content:" ” ";line-height:0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .left-aligned{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .right-aligned{text-align:right}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .center-aligned{text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .quotebox cite{display:block;font-style:normal}@media screen and (max-width:360px){.mw-parser-output .quotebox{min-width:100%;margin:0 0 0.8em!important;float:none!important}}</style>
<div class="quotebox-quote quoted left-aligned" style="">Gaul is divided into three parts, one of which the Belgae inhabit, the Aquitani another, those who in their own language are called Celts, in ours Gauls, the third.
(...) Of all these, the Belgae are the strongest (...) .</div>
<p><cite class="left-aligned" style="">— <a href="/wiki/Julius_Caesar" title="Julius Caesar">Julius Caesar</a>, De Bello Gallico, Book I, Ch. 1</cite>
</p>
</div>
<p>The <i><a href="/wiki/Belgae" title="Belgae">Belgae</a></i> were the inhabitants of the northernmost part of <a href="/wiki/Gaul" title="Gaul">Gaul</a>, which was significantly bigger than modern Belgium. Caesar used the word "<i>Belgium</i>" once, to refer to their region. <i><a href="/wiki/Gallia_Belgica" title="Gallia Belgica">Gallia Belgica</a></i>, as it was more commonly called, became a <a href="/wiki/Roman_province" title="Roman province">Roman province</a> as a result of his conquests. Areas closer to the Rhine frontier, including the eastern part of modern Belgium, eventually became part of the province of <i><a href="/wiki/Germania_Inferior" title="Germania Inferior">Germania Inferior</a></i>, which interacted with <a href="/wiki/Germanic_peoples" title="Germanic peoples">Germanic tribes</a> outside the empire. At the time when central government collapsed in the <a href="/wiki/Western_Roman_Empire" title="Western Roman Empire">Western Roman Empire</a>, the region of Belgium was inhabited by a mix of <a href="/wiki/Franks" title="Franks">Frankish</a> tribes and a more Romanized population. During the 5th century the area came under the rule of the <a href="/wiki/Merovingian" class="mw-redirect" title="Merovingian">Merovingian</a> kings, who had already seized power in what is northern France. A gradual shift of power during the 8th century led the kingdom of the Franks to evolve into the <a href="/wiki/Carolingian_Empire" title="Carolingian Empire">Carolingian Empire</a>.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Titian_-_Portrait_of_Charles_V_Seated_(cropped)_2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Titian_-_Portrait_of_Charles_V_Seated_%28cropped%29_2.jpg/180px-Titian_-_Portrait_of_Charles_V_Seated_%28cropped%29_2.jpg" decoding="async" width="180" height="231" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Titian_-_Portrait_of_Charles_V_Seated_%28cropped%29_2.jpg/270px-Titian_-_Portrait_of_Charles_V_Seated_%28cropped%29_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Titian_-_Portrait_of_Charles_V_Seated_%28cropped%29_2.jpg/360px-Titian_-_Portrait_of_Charles_V_Seated_%28cropped%29_2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="648" data-file-height="831" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Titian_-_Portrait_of_Charles_V_Seated_(cropped)_2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Charles_V,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Charles V, Holy Roman Emperor">Charles V, Holy Roman Emperor</a>, was born in <a href="/wiki/Ghent" title="Ghent">Ghent</a></div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Verdun" title="Treaty of Verdun">Treaty of Verdun</a> in 843 divided the Carolingian empire into three kingdoms, whose borders had a lasting impact on medieval political boundaries. Most of modern Belgium was in the <a href="/wiki/Middle_Francia" title="Middle Francia">Middle Kingdom</a>, later known as <a href="/wiki/Lotharingia" title="Lotharingia">Lotharingia</a>. Only the coastal county of Flanders became part of <a href="/wiki/West_Francia" title="West Francia">West Francia</a>, the predecessor of <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>. During the <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">Middle Ages</a>, Lotharingia came under the control of the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Holy Roman Emperor">Holy Roman Emperor</a>, but the lordships along the "March" (frontier) between the two great kingdoms maintained important connections.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_Burgundian_and_Habsburg_acquisitions_in_the_Low_Countries" title="Timeline of Burgundian and Habsburg acquisitions in the Low Countries">Many of these fiefdoms</a> were united in the <a href="/wiki/Burgundian_Netherlands" title="Burgundian Netherlands">Burgundian Netherlands</a> of the 14th and 15th centuries.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>
<a href="/wiki/Charles_V,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Charles V, Holy Roman Emperor">Emperor Charles&#160;V</a> extended the <a href="/wiki/Personal_union" title="Personal union">personal union</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Seventeen_Provinces" title="Seventeen Provinces">Seventeen Provinces</a> in the 1540s, making it far more than a personal union by the <a href="/wiki/Pragmatic_Sanction_of_1549" title="Pragmatic Sanction of 1549">Pragmatic Sanction of 1549</a> and increased his influence over the <a href="/wiki/Prince-Bishopric_of_Li%C3%A8ge" title="Prince-Bishopric of Liège">Prince-Bishopric of Liège</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Eighty_Years%27_War" title="Eighty Years&#39; War">Eighty Years' War</a> (1568–1648) divided the Low Countries into the northern <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Republic" title="Dutch Republic">United Provinces</a> (<i>Belgica Foederata</i> in <a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">Latin</a>, the "Federated Netherlands") and the <a href="/wiki/Southern_Netherlands" title="Southern Netherlands">Southern Netherlands</a> (<i>Belgica Regia</i>, the "Royal Netherlands"). The latter were ruled successively by the <a href="/wiki/Habsburg_Spain" title="Habsburg Spain">Spanish</a> (<a href="/wiki/Spanish_Netherlands" title="Spanish Netherlands">Spanish Netherlands</a>) and the <a href="/wiki/History_of_Austria#Charles_VI_and_Maria_Theresa_(1711–1780)" title="History of Austria">Austrian</a> <a href="/wiki/Habsburg" class="mw-redirect" title="Habsburg">Habsburgs</a> (<a href="/wiki/Austrian_Netherlands" title="Austrian Netherlands">Austrian Netherlands</a>) and comprised most of modern Belgium. This was the theatre of most <a href="/wiki/Franco-Spanish_War_(1635)" class="mw-redirect" title="Franco-Spanish War (1635)">Franco-Spanish</a> and <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Austrian_Succession" title="War of the Austrian Succession">Franco-Austrian wars</a> during the 17th and 18th centuries.
</p><p>Following the <a href="/wiki/French_Revolutionary_Wars:_Campaigns_of_1794" class="mw-redirect" title="French Revolutionary Wars: Campaigns of 1794">campaigns of 1794 in the French Revolutionary Wars</a>, the Low Countries—including territories that were never nominally under Habsburg rule, such as the Prince-Bishopric of Liège—were annexed by the <a href="/wiki/French_First_Republic" title="French First Republic">French First Republic</a>, ending Austrian rule in the region. The reunification of the Low Countries as the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_of_the_Netherlands" title="United Kingdom of the Netherlands">United Kingdom of the Netherlands</a> occurred at the dissolution of the <a href="/wiki/First_French_Empire" title="First French Empire">First French Empire</a> in 1814, after the abdication of Napoleon.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Independent_Belgium">Independent Belgium</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Wappers_-_Episodes_from_September_Days_1830_on_the_Place_de_l%E2%80%99H%C3%B4tel_de_Ville_in_Brussels.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Wappers_-_Episodes_from_September_Days_1830_on_the_Place_de_l%E2%80%99H%C3%B4tel_de_Ville_in_Brussels.JPG/220px-Wappers_-_Episodes_from_September_Days_1830_on_the_Place_de_l%E2%80%99H%C3%B4tel_de_Ville_in_Brussels.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="148" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Wappers_-_Episodes_from_September_Days_1830_on_the_Place_de_l%E2%80%99H%C3%B4tel_de_Ville_in_Brussels.JPG/330px-Wappers_-_Episodes_from_September_Days_1830_on_the_Place_de_l%E2%80%99H%C3%B4tel_de_Ville_in_Brussels.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Wappers_-_Episodes_from_September_Days_1830_on_the_Place_de_l%E2%80%99H%C3%B4tel_de_Ville_in_Brussels.JPG/440px-Wappers_-_Episodes_from_September_Days_1830_on_the_Place_de_l%E2%80%99H%C3%B4tel_de_Ville_in_Brussels.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3348" data-file-height="2250" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Wappers_-_Episodes_from_September_Days_1830_on_the_Place_de_l%E2%80%99H%C3%B4tel_de_Ville_in_Brussels.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Episode of the <a href="/wiki/Belgian_Revolution" title="Belgian Revolution">Belgian Revolution</a> of 1830 (1834), by <a href="/wiki/Gustaf_Wappers" title="Gustaf Wappers">Gustaf Wappers</a></div></div></div>
<p>In 1830, the <a href="/wiki/Belgian_Revolution" title="Belgian Revolution">Belgian Revolution</a> led to the separation of the Southern Provinces from the Netherlands and to the establishment of a Catholic and bourgeois, officially French-speaking and neutral, independent Belgium under a <a href="/wiki/Provisional_Government_of_Belgium" title="Provisional Government of Belgium">provisional government</a> and a <a href="/wiki/National_Congress_of_Belgium" title="National Congress of Belgium">national congress</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Dobbelaere-VoyE_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dobbelaere-VoyE-27">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Gooch_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gooch-28">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> Since the installation of <a href="/wiki/Leopold_I_of_Belgium" title="Leopold I of Belgium">Leopold&#160;I</a> as king on <span class="nowrap">21 July</span> 1831, now celebrated as Belgium's <a href="/wiki/National_Day" class="mw-redirect" title="National Day">National Day</a>, Belgium has been a <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_monarchy" title="Constitutional monarchy">constitutional monarchy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_democracy" class="mw-redirect" title="Parliamentary democracy">parliamentary democracy</a>, with a <a href="/wiki/La%C3%AFcit%C3%A9" title="Laïcité">laicist</a> constitution based on the <a href="/wiki/Napoleonic_code" class="mw-redirect" title="Napoleonic code">Napoleonic code</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> Although the franchise was initially restricted, <a href="/wiki/Universal_suffrage" title="Universal suffrage">universal suffrage</a> for men was introduced after the <a href="/wiki/Belgian_general_strike_of_1893" title="Belgian general strike of 1893">general strike of 1893</a> (with <a href="/wiki/Plural_voting" title="Plural voting">plural voting</a> until 1919) and for women in 1949.
</p><p>The main political parties of the 19th century were the <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Party_(Belgium)" title="Catholic Party (Belgium)">Catholic Party</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Liberal_Party_(Belgium)" title="Liberal Party (Belgium)">Liberal Party</a>, with the <a href="/wiki/Belgian_Labour_Party" title="Belgian Labour Party">Belgian Labour Party</a> emerging towards the end of the 19th century. French was originally the single official language adopted by the <a href="/wiki/Nobility" title="Nobility">nobility</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Bourgeoisie" title="Bourgeoisie">bourgeoisie</a>. It progressively lost its overall importance as Dutch became recognized as well. This recognition became official in 1898 and in 1967 the parliament accepted a Dutch version of the <a href="/wiki/Belgian_Constitution" class="mw-redirect" title="Belgian Constitution">Constitution</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Berlin_Conference" title="Berlin Conference">Berlin Conference</a> of 1885 ceded control of the <a href="/wiki/Congo_Free_State" title="Congo Free State">Congo Free State</a> to <a href="/wiki/Leopold_II_of_Belgium" title="Leopold II of Belgium">King Leopold&#160;II</a> as his private possession. From around 1900 there was growing international concern for the <a href="/wiki/Atrocities_in_the_Congo_Free_State" title="Atrocities in the Congo Free State">extreme and savage treatment of the Congolese population under Leopold&#160;II</a>, for whom the Congo was primarily a source of revenue from ivory and rubber production.<sup id="cite_ref-Forbath_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Forbath-31">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> Many Congolese were killed by Leopold's agents for failing to meet production quotas for ivory and rubber.<sup id="cite_ref-nytimes.com_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nytimes.com-32">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> It is estimated that nearly 10&#160;million were killed during the Leopold period. In 1908, this outcry led the Belgian state to assume responsibility for the government of the colony, henceforth called the <a href="/wiki/Belgian_Congo" title="Belgian Congo">Belgian Congo</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> A Belgian commission in 1919 estimated that Congo's population was half what it was in 1879.<sup id="cite_ref-nytimes.com_32-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nytimes.com-32">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Cheering_crowds_greet_British_troops_entering_Brussels,_4_September_1944._BU483.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Cheering_crowds_greet_British_troops_entering_Brussels%2C_4_September_1944._BU483.jpg/220px-Cheering_crowds_greet_British_troops_entering_Brussels%2C_4_September_1944._BU483.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="221" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Cheering_crowds_greet_British_troops_entering_Brussels%2C_4_September_1944._BU483.jpg/330px-Cheering_crowds_greet_British_troops_entering_Brussels%2C_4_September_1944._BU483.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Cheering_crowds_greet_British_troops_entering_Brussels%2C_4_September_1944._BU483.jpg/440px-Cheering_crowds_greet_British_troops_entering_Brussels%2C_4_September_1944._BU483.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1772" data-file-height="1781" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Cheering_crowds_greet_British_troops_entering_Brussels,_4_September_1944._BU483.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Cheering crowds greet British troops entering <a href="/wiki/Brussels" title="Brussels">Brussels</a>, 4 September 1944</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/German_invasion_of_Belgium" title="German invasion of Belgium">Germany invaded Belgium in August 1914</a> as part of the <a href="/wiki/Schlieffen_Plan" title="Schlieffen Plan">Schlieffen Plan</a> to attack <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>, and much of the <a href="/wiki/Western_Front_(World_War_I)" title="Western Front (World War I)">Western Front</a> fighting of <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a> occurred in western parts of the country. The opening months of the war were known as the <a href="/wiki/Rape_of_Belgium" title="Rape of Belgium">Rape of Belgium</a> due to German excesses. Belgium assumed control of the <a href="/wiki/German_colonies" class="mw-redirect" title="German colonies">German colonies</a> of <a href="/wiki/Ruanda-Urundi" title="Ruanda-Urundi">Ruanda-Urundi</a> (modern-day <a href="/wiki/Rwanda" title="Rwanda">Rwanda</a> and <a href="/wiki/Burundi" title="Burundi">Burundi</a>) during the war, and in 1924 the <a href="/wiki/League_of_Nations" title="League of Nations">League of Nations</a> mandated them to Belgium. In the aftermath of the First World War, Belgium annexed the <a href="/wiki/Districts_of_Prussia" title="Districts of Prussia">Prussian districts</a> of <a href="/wiki/Eupen-Malmedy" title="Eupen-Malmedy">Eupen and Malmedy</a> in 1925, thereby causing the presence of a German-speaking minority.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Belgium" title="Battle of Belgium">German forces again invaded the country in May 1940</a>, and 40,690 Belgians, over half of them Jews, were killed during the subsequent <a href="/wiki/German_occupation_of_Belgium_during_World_War_II" title="German occupation of Belgium during World War II">occupation</a> and <a href="/wiki/The_Holocaust_in_Belgium" title="The Holocaust in Belgium">The Holocaust</a>. From September 1944 to February 1945 <a href="/wiki/Allied_advance_from_Paris_to_the_Rhine" title="Allied advance from Paris to the Rhine">the Allies liberated</a> Belgium. After World War&#160;II, <a href="/wiki/General_strike_against_Leopold_III_of_Belgium" class="mw-redirect" title="General strike against Leopold III of Belgium">a general strike</a> forced King <a href="/wiki/Leopold_III_of_Belgium" title="Leopold III of Belgium">Leopold&#160;III</a> to abdicate in 1951, since <a href="/wiki/Royal_Question" title="Royal Question">many Belgians felt he had collaborated with Germany</a> during the war.<sup id="cite_ref-Arango_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Arango-34">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> The Belgian Congo gained independence in 1960 during the <a href="/wiki/Congo_Crisis" title="Congo Crisis">Congo Crisis</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> Ruanda-Urundi followed with its independence two years later. Belgium joined <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a> as a founding member and formed the Benelux group of nations with the Netherlands and Luxembourg.
</p><p>Belgium became one of the six founding members of the <a href="/wiki/European_Coal_and_Steel_Community" title="European Coal and Steel Community">European Coal and Steel Community</a> in 1951 and of the <a href="/wiki/European_Atomic_Energy_Community" title="European Atomic Energy Community">European Atomic Energy Community</a> and <a href="/wiki/European_Economic_Community" title="European Economic Community">European Economic Community</a>, established in 1957. The latter has now become the European Union, for which Belgium hosts major administrations and institutions, including the <a href="/wiki/European_Commission" title="European Commission">European Commission</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Council_of_the_European_Union" title="Council of the European Union">Council of the European Union</a> and the extraordinary and committee sessions of the <a href="/wiki/European_Parliament" title="European Parliament">European Parliament</a>.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Belgium" title="Geography of Belgium">Geography of Belgium</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:322px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Belgium_relief_location_map.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Belgium_relief_location_map.jpg/320px-Belgium_relief_location_map.jpg" decoding="async" width="320" height="278" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Belgium_relief_location_map.jpg/480px-Belgium_relief_location_map.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Belgium_relief_location_map.jpg/640px-Belgium_relief_location_map.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1136" data-file-height="988" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Belgium_relief_location_map.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A relief map of Belgium</div></div></div>
<p>Belgium shares borders with <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a> (<span class="nowrap">620&#160;km</span>), <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a> (<span class="nowrap">167&#160;km</span>), <a href="/wiki/Luxembourg" title="Luxembourg">Luxembourg</a> (<span class="nowrap">148&#160;km</span>) and the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Netherlands</a> (<span class="nowrap">450&#160;km</span>). Its total surface, including water area, is 30,688&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (11,849&#160;sq&#160;mi). Before 2018, its total area was believed to be 30,528&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (11,787&#160;sq&#160;mi). However, when the country's statistics were measured in 2018, a new calculation method was used. Unlike previous calculations, this one included the area from the coast to the low-water line, revealing the country to be 160&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (62&#160;sq&#160;mi) larger in surface area than previously thought.<sup id="cite_ref-statbel_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-statbel-36">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-hetlaatste_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hetlaatste-37">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> Its land area alone is 30,278&#160;km<sup>2</sup>.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-38">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The land area alone is likely greater now that the total surface has been discovered to be 168 kilometers greater (February 2019)">needs update</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> It lies between latitudes 49°30' and 51°30' N, and longitudes 2°33' and 6°24' E.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Teut104.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Teut104.jpg/220px-Teut104.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Teut104.jpg/330px-Teut104.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Teut104.jpg/440px-Teut104.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Teut104.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Campine" title="Campine">Campine</a> landscape.</div></div></div>
<p>Belgium has three main geographical regions; the coastal plain in the northwest and the central plateau both belong to the Anglo-Belgian Basin, and the <a href="/wiki/Ardennes" title="Ardennes">Ardennes</a> uplands in the southeast to the <a href="/wiki/Variscan_orogeny" title="Variscan orogeny">Hercynian orogenic belt</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Paris_Basin" title="Paris Basin">Paris Basin</a> reaches a small fourth area at Belgium's southernmost tip, <a href="/wiki/Belgian_Lorraine" title="Belgian Lorraine">Belgian Lorraine</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The coastal plain consists mainly of sand dunes and <a href="/wiki/Polder" title="Polder">polders</a>. Further inland lies a smooth, slowly rising landscape irrigated by numerous waterways, with fertile valleys and the northeastern sandy plain of the <a href="/wiki/Campine" title="Campine">Campine</a> (<i>Kempen</i>). The thickly forested hills and plateaus of the Ardennes are more rugged and rocky with caves and small <a href="/wiki/Canyon" title="Canyon">gorges</a>. Extending westward into France, this area is eastwardly connected to the <a href="/wiki/Eifel" title="Eifel">Eifel</a> in Germany by the <a href="/wiki/High_Fens" title="High Fens">High Fens</a> plateau, on which the <a href="/wiki/Signal_de_Botrange" title="Signal de Botrange">Signal de Botrange</a> forms the country's highest point at 694&#160;m (2,277&#160;ft).<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Anseremme_-_Fre%C3%BFr_051011_(1).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Anseremme_-_Fre%C3%BFr_051011_%281%29.jpg/220px-Anseremme_-_Fre%C3%BFr_051011_%281%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Anseremme_-_Fre%C3%BFr_051011_%281%29.jpg/330px-Anseremme_-_Fre%C3%BFr_051011_%281%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Anseremme_-_Fre%C3%BFr_051011_%281%29.jpg/440px-Anseremme_-_Fre%C3%BFr_051011_%281%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2272" data-file-height="1704" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Anseremme_-_Fre%C3%BFr_051011_(1).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Meuse" title="Meuse">Meuse</a> river between <a href="/wiki/Dinant" title="Dinant">Dinant</a> and Hastière.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Hautes-Fagnes.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Hautes-Fagnes.jpg/220px-Hautes-Fagnes.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Hautes-Fagnes.jpg/330px-Hautes-Fagnes.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Hautes-Fagnes.jpg/440px-Hautes-Fagnes.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2272" data-file-height="1704" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Hautes-Fagnes.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/High_Fens" title="High Fens">High Fens</a> landscape near the German border.</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Climate_of_Belgium" class="mw-redirect" title="Climate of Belgium">The climate</a> is <a href="/wiki/Oceanic_climate" title="Oceanic climate">maritime temperate</a> with significant precipitation in all seasons (<a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">Köppen climate classification</a>: <i>Cfb</i>), like most of northwest Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> The average temperature is lowest in January at 3&#160;°C (37.4&#160;°F) and highest in July at 18&#160;°C (64.4&#160;°F). The average precipitation per month varies between 54&#160;mm (2.1&#160;in) for February and April, to 78&#160;mm (3.1&#160;in) for July.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> Averages for the years 2000 to 2006 show daily temperature minimums of 7&#160;°C (44.6&#160;°F) and maximums of 14&#160;°C (57.2&#160;°F) and monthly rainfall of 74&#160;mm (2.9&#160;in); these are about 1&#160;°C and nearly 10 millimetres above last century's normal values, respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-statbel2_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-statbel2-45">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Phytogeography" title="Phytogeography">Phytogeographically</a>, Belgium is shared between the Atlantic European and Central European provinces of the <a href="/wiki/Circumboreal_Region" title="Circumboreal Region">Circumboreal Region</a> within the <a href="/wiki/Boreal_Kingdom" title="Boreal Kingdom">Boreal Kingdom</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> According to the <a href="/wiki/World_Wide_Fund_for_Nature" title="World Wide Fund for Nature">World Wide Fund for Nature</a>, the territory of Belgium belongs to the <a href="/wiki/Ecoregion" title="Ecoregion">ecoregion</a> of Atlantic mixed forests.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> Because of its high population density, industrialization and its location in the center of Western Europe, Belgium still faces some <a href="/wiki/Environment_of_Belgium" title="Environment of Belgium">environmental problems</a>. However, due to consistent efforts by the various levels of government in Belgium, the state of the environment in Belgium is gradually improving. This led to Belgium being ranked as <a href="/wiki/Environmental_Performance_Index" title="Environmental Performance Index">one of the top 10 countries</a> (9 out of 132) in terms of environmental protection trends, and to Belgium being ranked in 2012 as the 24th country out of 132 for environmental protection. Belgium moreover has one of Europe's highest waste recycling rates. In particular, the Flemish region of Belgium has the highest waste diversion rate in Europe. Almost 75 percent of the residential waste produced there is reused, recycled, or composted.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Provinces">Provinces</span></h3>

</div></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Provinces_of_Belgium" title="Provinces of Belgium">Provinces of Belgium</a></div>
<p>The territory of Belgium is divided into three Regions, two of which, the <a href="/wiki/Flemish_Region" title="Flemish Region">Flemish Region</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wallonia" title="Wallonia">Walloon Region</a>, are in turn subdivided into <a href="/wiki/Provinces_of_Belgium" title="Provinces of Belgium">provinces</a>; the third Region, the <a href="/wiki/Brussels_Capital_Region" class="mw-redirect" title="Brussels Capital Region">Brussels Capital Region</a>, is neither a province nor a part of a province.
</p>
