<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Belgium" title="Politics of Belgium">Politics of Belgium</a> and <a href="/wiki/Belgian_federal_government" class="mw-redirect" title="Belgian federal government">Belgian federal government</a></div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r889293853/mw-parser-output/.tmulti">.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{display:flex;flex-direction:column}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{display:flex;flex-direction:row;clear:left;flex-wrap:wrap;width:100%;box-sizing:border-box}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{margin:1px;float:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .theader{clear:both;font-weight:bold;text-align:center;align-self:center;background-color:transparent;width:100%}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbcaption{text-align:left;background-color:transparent}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-left{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-right{text-align:right}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-center{text-align:center}@media all and (max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;max-width:none!important;align-items:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{justify-content:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{float:none!important;max-width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbcaption{text-align:center}}</style><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:303px;max-width:303px"><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:127px;max-width:127px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Koning_Filip_van_Belgi%C3%AB.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Koning_Filip_van_Belgi%C3%AB.jpg/125px-Koning_Filip_van_Belgi%C3%AB.jpg" decoding="async" width="125" height="192" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Koning_Filip_van_Belgi%C3%AB.jpg/188px-Koning_Filip_van_Belgi%C3%AB.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Koning_Filip_van_Belgi%C3%AB.jpg/250px-Koning_Filip_van_Belgi%C3%AB.jpg 2x" data-file-width="790" data-file-height="1213" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption"><a href="/wiki/Philippe_of_Belgium" title="Philippe of Belgium">Philippe</a><br /><span style="font-size:85%;"><a href="/wiki/Monarchy_of_Belgium" title="Monarchy of Belgium">King of the Belgians</a> since 2013</span></div></div><div class="tsingle" style="width:172px;max-width:172px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Charles_Michel_(politician).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Charles_Michel_%28politician%29.jpg/170px-Charles_Michel_%28politician%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="192" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Charles_Michel_%28politician%29.jpg/255px-Charles_Michel_%28politician%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Charles_Michel_%28politician%29.jpg/340px-Charles_Michel_%28politician%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="700" data-file-height="790" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption"><a href="/wiki/Charles_Michel" title="Charles Michel">Charles Michel</a><br /><span style="font-size:85%;"><a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Belgium" title="Prime Minister of Belgium">Prime Minister</a> since 2014</span></div></div></div></div></div>
<p>Belgium is a <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_monarchy" title="Constitutional monarchy">constitutional</a>, <a href="/wiki/Popular_monarchy" title="Popular monarchy">popular monarchy</a> and a <a href="/wiki/Federalism" title="Federalism">federal</a> <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_system" title="Parliamentary system">parliamentary democracy</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Bicameralism" title="Bicameralism">bicameral</a> <a href="/wiki/Belgian_Federal_Parliament" title="Belgian Federal Parliament">federal parliament</a> is composed of a <a href="/wiki/Senate_(Belgium)" title="Senate (Belgium)">Senate</a> and a <a href="/wiki/Chamber_of_Representatives_(Belgium)" title="Chamber of Representatives (Belgium)">Chamber of Representatives</a>. The former is made up of 50 senators appointed by the parliaments of the <a href="/wiki/Communities,_regions_and_language_areas_of_Belgium" title="Communities, regions and language areas of Belgium">communities and regions</a> and 10 <a href="/wiki/Belgian_Senate#Co-opted_Senators" class="mw-redirect" title="Belgian Senate">co-opted senators</a>. Prior to 2014, most of the Senate's members were directly elected. The <a href="/wiki/Chambers_of_parliament" class="mw-redirect" title="Chambers of parliament">Chamber</a>'s 150 representatives are elected under a <a href="/wiki/Proportional_voting" class="mw-redirect" title="Proportional voting">proportional voting</a> system from 11 <a href="/wiki/Arrondissements_of_Belgium" title="Arrondissements of Belgium">electoral districts</a>. Belgium has <a href="/wiki/Compulsory_voting" title="Compulsory voting">compulsory voting</a> and thus maintains one of the highest rates of <a href="/wiki/Voter_turnout" title="Voter turnout">voter turnout</a> in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-Franklin_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Franklin-48">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Monarchy_of_Belgium" title="Monarchy of Belgium">King</a> (currently <a href="/wiki/Philippe_of_Belgium" title="Philippe of Belgium">Philippe</a>) is the <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">head of state</a>, though with limited <a href="/wiki/Royal_Prerogative" class="mw-redirect" title="Royal Prerogative">prerogatives</a>. He appoints ministers, including a Prime Minister, that have the confidence of the <a href="/wiki/Chamber_of_Representatives_of_Belgium" class="mw-redirect" title="Chamber of Representatives of Belgium">Chamber of Representatives</a> to form the <a href="/wiki/Federal_government" class="mw-redirect" title="Federal government">federal government</a>. The Council of Ministers is composed of no more than fifteen members. With the possible exception of the Prime Minister, the Council of Ministers is composed of an equal number of Dutch-speaking members and French-speaking members.<sup id="cite_ref-constitution1_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-constitution1-49">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup>
The judicial system is based on <a href="/wiki/Civil_law_(legal_system)" title="Civil law (legal system)">civil law</a> and originates from the <a href="/wiki/Napoleonic_code" class="mw-redirect" title="Napoleonic code">Napoleonic code</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Court_of_Cassation_(Belgium)" title="Court of Cassation (Belgium)">Court of Cassation</a> is the court of last resort, with the <a href="/wiki/Court_of_appeal_(Belgium)" title="Court of appeal (Belgium)">courts of appeal</a> one level below.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Political_culture">Political culture</span></h3>
<p>Belgium's political institutions are complex; <a href="/wiki/Pillarisation" title="Pillarisation">most political power is organized around the need to represent the main cultural communities</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup>
Since about 1970, the significant national <a href="/wiki/Political_parties_in_Belgium" title="Political parties in Belgium">Belgian political parties</a> have split into distinct components that mainly represent the political and linguistic interests of these communities.<sup id="cite_ref-USStateDpt_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USStateDpt-52">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup>
The major parties in each community, though close to the political center, belong to three main groups: <a href="/wiki/Christian_democracy" title="Christian democracy">Christian Democrats</a>, <a href="/wiki/Liberalism_in_Belgium" title="Liberalism in Belgium">Liberals</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Social_democracy" title="Social democracy">Social Democrats</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup>
Further notable parties came into being well after the middle of last century, mainly around <a href="/wiki/List_of_political_parties_in_Belgium#Linguistic_parties" class="mw-redirect" title="List of political parties in Belgium">linguistic</a>, nationalist, or environmental themes and recently smaller ones of some specific liberal nature.<sup id="cite_ref-USStateDpt_52-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USStateDpt-52">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Brussel_Parlementsgebouw.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Brussel_Parlementsgebouw.jpg/220px-Brussel_Parlementsgebouw.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Brussel_Parlementsgebouw.jpg/330px-Brussel_Parlementsgebouw.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Brussel_Parlementsgebouw.jpg/440px-Brussel_Parlementsgebouw.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="600" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Brussel_Parlementsgebouw.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Belgian_Federal_Parliament" title="Belgian Federal Parliament">Belgian Federal Parliament</a> in <a href="/wiki/Brussels" title="Brussels">Brussels</a>, one of <a href="/wiki/List_of_governments_in_Belgium" title="List of governments in Belgium">six different governments</a> of the country</div></div></div>
<p>A string of Christian Democrat coalition governments from 1958 <a href="/wiki/Belgian_federal_election,_1999" class="mw-redirect" title="Belgian federal election, 1999">was broken in 1999</a> after the first <a href="/wiki/Dioxine_affair" class="mw-redirect" title="Dioxine affair">dioxin crisis</a>, a major <a href="/wiki/Food_contaminant" title="Food contaminant">food contamination</a> scandal.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> A "rainbow coalition" emerged from six parties: the Flemish and the French-speaking Liberals, Social Democrats and Greens.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> Later, a "<a href="/wiki/Purple_(government)" title="Purple (government)">purple coalition</a>" of Liberals and Social Democrats formed after the Greens lost most of their seats in the <a href="/wiki/Belgian_federal_election,_2003" class="mw-redirect" title="Belgian federal election, 2003">2003 election</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The government led by Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Guy_Verhofstadt" title="Guy Verhofstadt">Guy Verhofstadt</a> from 1999 to 2007 achieved a balanced budget, some <a href="/wiki/Tax_reform" title="Tax reform">tax reforms</a>, a labor-market reform, scheduled <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_energy_policy#Europe" title="Nuclear energy policy">nuclear phase-out</a> and instigated legislation allowing more stringent <a href="/wiki/War_Crimes_Law_(Belgium)" title="War Crimes Law (Belgium)">war crime</a> and more lenient <a href="/wiki/Drug_harmfulness" title="Drug harmfulness">soft drug usage</a> prosecution. Restrictions on withholding <a href="/wiki/Euthanasia" title="Euthanasia">euthanasia</a> were reduced and <a href="/wiki/Same-sex_marriage_in_Belgium" title="Same-sex marriage in Belgium">same-sex marriage</a> legalized. The government promoted active diplomacy in Africa<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Governmental_positions_on_the_Iraq_War_prior_to_the_2003_invasion_of_Iraq" title="Governmental positions on the Iraq War prior to the 2003 invasion of Iraq">opposed the invasion of Iraq</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> It is the only country that does not have age restrictions on euthanasia.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc-61">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Verhofstadt's coalition fared badly in the <a href="/wiki/Belgian_federal_election,_2007" class="mw-redirect" title="Belgian federal election, 2007">June 2007 elections</a>. For more than a year, the country experienced a <a href="/wiki/2007_Belgian_government_formation" class="mw-redirect" title="2007 Belgian government formation">political crisis</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> This crisis was such that many observers speculated on a possible <a href="/wiki/Partition_of_Belgium" title="Partition of Belgium">partition of Belgium</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-SanFranChro_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SanFranChro-63">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BBCJuly2008_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBCJuly2008-64">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Telegraph2010_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Telegraph2010-65">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> From <span class="nowrap">21 December</span> 2007 until <span class="nowrap">20 March</span> 2008 the temporary <a href="/wiki/Verhofstadt_III_Government" title="Verhofstadt III Government">Verhofstadt&#160;III Government</a> was in office. This coalition of the <a href="/wiki/Christen-Democratisch_en_Vlaams" title="Christen-Democratisch en Vlaams">Flemish</a> and <a href="/wiki/Humanist_Democratic_Centre" class="mw-redirect" title="Humanist Democratic Centre">Francophone Christian Democrats</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Open_Vlaamse_Liberalen_en_Democraten" title="Open Vlaamse Liberalen en Democraten">Flemish</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mouvement_R%C3%A9formateur" title="Mouvement Réformateur">Francophone Liberals</a> together with the <a href="/wiki/Socialist_Party_(francophone_Belgium)" class="mw-redirect" title="Socialist Party (francophone Belgium)">Francophone Social Democrats</a> was an interim government until <span class="nowrap">20 March</span> 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-news_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-news-66">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On that day a <a href="/wiki/Leterme_I_Government" title="Leterme I Government">new government</a>, led by Flemish Christian Democrat <a href="/wiki/Yves_Leterme" title="Yves Leterme">Yves Leterme</a>, the actual winner of the federal elections of <span class="nowrap">June 2007</span>, was sworn in by the king. On <span class="nowrap">15 July</span> 2008 Leterme announced the resignation of the cabinet to the king, as no progress in <a href="/wiki/State_reform_in_Belgium" title="State reform in Belgium">constitutional reforms</a> had been made.<sup id="cite_ref-news_66-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-news-66">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>
In December 2008 he once more offered his resignation to the king after a <a href="/wiki/2008%E2%80%932009_Belgian_financial_crisis" class="mw-redirect" title="2008–2009 Belgian financial crisis">crisis</a> surrounding the sale of <a href="/wiki/Fortis_(finance)" title="Fortis (finance)">Fortis</a> to <a href="/wiki/BNP_Paribas" title="BNP Paribas">BNP Paribas</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> At this juncture, his resignation was accepted and <a href="/wiki/Christen-Democratisch_en_Vlaams" title="Christen-Democratisch en Vlaams">Christian Democratic and Flemish</a> <a href="/wiki/Herman_Van_Rompuy" title="Herman Van Rompuy">Herman Van Rompuy</a> was sworn in as Prime Minister on <span class="nowrap">30 December</span> 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>After Herman Van Rompuy was designated the first permanent <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_European_Council" title="President of the European Council">President of the European Council</a> on <span class="nowrap">19 November</span> 2009, he offered the resignation of his government to King Albert&#160;II on <span class="nowrap">25 November</span> 2009. A few hours later, the <a href="/wiki/Leterme_II_Government" title="Leterme II Government">new government</a> under Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Yves_Leterme" title="Yves Leterme">Yves Leterme</a> was sworn in. On <span class="nowrap">22 April</span> 2010, Leterme again offered the resignation of his cabinet to the king<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> after one of the coalition partners, the <a href="/wiki/OpenVLD" class="mw-redirect" title="OpenVLD">OpenVLD</a>, withdrew from the government, and on <span class="nowrap">26 April</span> 2010 King Albert officially accepted the resignation.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Parliamentary elections in Belgium on <span class="nowrap">13 June</span> 2010 saw the Flemish nationalist <a href="/wiki/New_Flemish_Alliance" title="New Flemish Alliance">N-VA</a> become the largest party in Flanders, and the Socialist Party PS the largest party in Wallonia.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> Until December 2011, Belgium was governed by Leterme's <a href="/wiki/Caretaker_government" title="Caretaker government">caretaker government</a> awaiting the end of the deadlocked negotiations for <a href="/wiki/2010%E2%80%932011_Belgian_government_formation" class="mw-redirect" title="2010–2011 Belgian government formation">formation of a new government</a>. By 30 March 2011 this set a new world record for the elapsed time without an official government, previously held by war-torn <a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq">Iraq</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_News_6_May_2015_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_News_6_May_2015-72">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> Finally, in December 2011 the <a href="/wiki/Di_Rupo_Government" title="Di Rupo Government">Di Rupo Government</a> led by Walloon socialist Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Elio_Di_Rupo" title="Elio Di Rupo">Elio Di Rupo</a> was sworn in.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Belgian_federal_election,_2014" class="mw-redirect" title="Belgian federal election, 2014">2014 federal election</a> (coinciding with the <a href="/wiki/Belgian_regional_elections,_2014" class="mw-redirect" title="Belgian regional elections, 2014">regional elections</a>) resulted in a further electoral gain for the Flemish nationalist N-VA, although the incumbent coalition (composed of Flemish and French-speaking Social Democrats, Liberals, and Christian Democrats) maintains a solid majority in Parliament and in all electoral constituencies. On 22 July 2014, King Philippe nominated <a href="/wiki/Charles_Michel" title="Charles Michel">Charles Michel</a> (MR) and <a href="/wiki/Kris_Peeters" title="Kris Peeters">Kris Peeters</a> (CD&amp;V) to <a href="/wiki/2014_Belgian_government_formation" title="2014 Belgian government formation">lead the formation of a new federal cabinet</a> composed of the Flemish parties N-VA, CD&amp;V, Open Vld and the French-speaking MR, which resulted in the <a href="/wiki/Michel_I_Government" title="Michel I Government">Michel Government</a>. It is the first time N-VA is part of the federal cabinet, while the French-speaking side is represented only by the MR, which achieved a minority of the public votes in Wallonia.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Communities_and_regions">Communities and regions</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Communities,_regions_and_language_areas_of_Belgium" title="Communities, regions and language areas of Belgium">Communities, regions and language areas of Belgium</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Communities_of_Belgium.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Communities_of_Belgium.svg/220px-Communities_of_Belgium.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="180" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Communities_of_Belgium.svg/330px-Communities_of_Belgium.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Communities_of_Belgium.svg/440px-Communities_of_Belgium.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="307" data-file-height="251" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Communities_of_Belgium.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Communities:<br /><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #fab274; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Flemish_Community" title="Flemish Community">Flemish Community</a> / Dutch language area</div> <div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="margin:1px 0; display:inline-block; border:1px solid black; background-color:#f2536b; color:black"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:0.1em; height:0em; border-left: 1.5em solid #fab274; border-bottom: 1.51em solid #f2536b;">&#160;</span></span>&#160;Flemish &amp; French Community / bilingual language area</div> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #f2536b; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/French_Community_of_Belgium" title="French Community of Belgium">French Community</a> / French language area</div><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #40bb6a; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/German-speaking_Community_of_Belgium" title="German-speaking Community of Belgium">German-speaking Community</a> / German language area</div></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Regions_of_Belgium.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Regions_of_Belgium.svg/220px-Regions_of_Belgium.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="180" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Regions_of_Belgium.svg/330px-Regions_of_Belgium.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Regions_of_Belgium.svg/440px-Regions_of_Belgium.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="307" data-file-height="251" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Regions_of_Belgium.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Regions:<br /><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #fab274; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Flemish_Region" title="Flemish Region">Flemish Region</a> / Dutch language area</div><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #2385d2; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Brussels" title="Brussels">Brussels</a>-Capital Region / bilingual area</div><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #f2536b; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Wallonia" title="Wallonia">Walloon Region</a> / French and German language areas</div></div></div></div>
<p>Following a usage which can be traced back to the Burgundian and Habsburg courts,<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> in the 19th century it was necessary to speak French to belong to the governing upper class, and those who could only speak Dutch were effectively second-class citizens.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> Late that century, and continuing into the 20th century, <a href="/wiki/Flemish_movement" class="mw-redirect" title="Flemish movement">Flemish movements</a> evolved to counter this situation.<sup id="cite_ref-Fitzmaurice1996-p31_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fitzmaurice1996-p31-75">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>While the people in Southern Belgium spoke French or dialects of French, and <a href="/wiki/Frenchification_of_Brussels" class="mw-redirect" title="Frenchification of Brussels">most Brusselers adopted French</a> as their first language, the Flemings refused to do so and succeeded progressively in making Dutch an equal language in the education system.<sup id="cite_ref-Fitzmaurice1996-p31_75-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fitzmaurice1996-p31-75">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> Following World War&#160;II, Belgian politics became increasingly dominated by the autonomy of its two main linguistic communities.<sup id="cite_ref-EED_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EED-76">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> Intercommunal tensions rose and the constitution was amended to minimize the potential for conflict.<sup id="cite_ref-EED_76-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EED-76">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Based on the four language areas defined in 1962–63 (the Dutch, bilingual, French and German language areas), consecutive <a href="/wiki/State_reform_in_Belgium" title="State reform in Belgium">revisions</a> of <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Belgium" title="Constitution of Belgium">the country's constitution</a> in 1970, 1980, 1988 and 1993 established a unique form of a federal state with segregated political power into three levels:<sup id="cite_ref-rolandwillemyns_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rolandwillemyns-77">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-constitution2_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-constitution2-78">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<ol><li>The <a href="/wiki/Belgian_federal_government" class="mw-redirect" title="Belgian federal government">federal government</a>, based in Brussels.</li>
<li>The three language communities:
<ul><li>the <a href="/wiki/Flemish_Community" title="Flemish Community">Flemish Community</a> (Dutch-speaking);</li>
<li>the <a href="/wiki/French_Community_of_Belgium" title="French Community of Belgium">French Community</a> (French-speaking);</li>
<li>the <a href="/wiki/German-speaking_Community_of_Belgium" title="German-speaking Community of Belgium">German-speaking Community</a>.</li></ul></li>
<li>The three regions:
<ul><li>the <a href="/wiki/Flemish_Region" title="Flemish Region">Flemish Region</a>, subdivided into five <a href="/wiki/Provinces_of_Belgium" title="Provinces of Belgium">provinces</a>;</li>
<li>the <a href="/wiki/Wallonia" title="Wallonia">Walloon Region</a>, subdivided into five provinces;</li>
<li>the <a href="/wiki/Brussels-Capital_Region" class="mw-redirect" title="Brussels-Capital Region">Brussels-Capital Region</a>.</li></ul></li></ol>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Language_legislation_in_Belgium" title="Language legislation in Belgium">constitutional language areas</a> determine the official languages in their municipalities, as well as the geographical limits of the empowered institutions for specific matters.<sup id="cite_ref-Fitzmaurice1996-p121_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fitzmaurice1996-p121-79">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> Although this would allow for seven parliaments and governments when the Communities and Regions were created in 1980, Flemish politicians decided to merge both.<sup id="cite_ref-Fitzmaurice1996-p122_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fitzmaurice1996-p122-80">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> Thus the Flemings just have one single institutional body of parliament and government is empowered for all except federal and specific municipal matters.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;C&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The overlapping boundaries of the Regions and Communities have created two notable peculiarities: the territory of the Brussels-Capital Region (which came into existence nearly a decade after the other regions) is included in both the Flemish and French Communities, and the territory of the German-speaking Community lies wholly within the Walloon Region. Conflicts about jurisdiction between the bodies are resolved by the <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_Court_of_Belgium" class="mw-redirect" title="Constitutional Court of Belgium">Constitutional Court of Belgium</a>. The structure is intended as a compromise to allow different cultures to live together peacefully.<sup id="cite_ref-Fitzmaurice_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fitzmaurice-13">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Locus_of_policy_jurisdiction">Locus of policy jurisdiction</span></h3>
<p>The Federal State's authority includes justice, defense, federal police, social security, nuclear energy, monetary policy and public debt, and other aspects of public finances. State-owned companies include the <a href="/wiki/Belgian_Post_Group" class="mw-redirect" title="Belgian Post Group">Belgian Post Group</a> and <a href="/wiki/National_Railway_Company_of_Belgium" title="National Railway Company of Belgium">Belgian Railways</a>. The Federal Government is responsible for the obligations of Belgium and its federalized institutions towards the European Union and NATO. It controls substantial parts of public health, home affairs and foreign affairs.<sup id="cite_ref-fedgov1_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fedgov1-82">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> The budget—without the debt—controlled by the federal government amounts to about 50% of the national fiscal income. The federal government employs around 12% of the civil servants.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Communities exercise their authority only within linguistically determined geographical boundaries, originally oriented towards the individuals of a Community's language: culture (including audiovisual media), education and the use of the relevant language. Extensions to personal matters less directly connected with language comprise health policy (curative and preventive medicine) and assistance to individuals (protection of youth, social welfare, aid to families, <a href="/wiki/Immigrant" class="mw-redirect" title="Immigrant">immigrant</a> assistance services, and so on.).<sup id="cite_ref-fedgov2_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fedgov2-84">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Regions have authority in fields that can be broadly associated with their territory. These include economy, employment, agriculture, water policy, housing, public works, energy, transport, the environment, town and country planning, nature conservation, credit and foreign trade. They supervise the provinces, municipalities and intercommunal utility companies.<sup id="cite_ref-fedgov3_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fedgov3-85">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In several fields, the different levels each have their own say on specifics. With education, for instance, the autonomy of the Communities neither includes decisions about the compulsory aspect nor allows for setting minimum requirements for awarding qualifications, which remain federal matters.<sup id="cite_ref-fedgov1_82-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fedgov1-82">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> Each level of government can be involved in scientific research and international relations associated with its powers. The treaty-making power of the Regions' and Communities' Governments is the broadest of all the Federating units of all the Federations all over the world.<sup id="cite_ref-Lagasse1_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lagasse1-86">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Lagasse2_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lagasse2-87">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Suinen_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Suinen-88">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">Foreign relations</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Belgium" title="Foreign relations of Belgium">Foreign relations of Belgium</a></div>
<p>Because of its location at the crossroads of <a href="/wiki/Western_Europe" title="Western Europe">Western Europe</a>, Belgium has historically been the route of invading armies from its larger neighbors. With virtually defenseless borders, Belgium has traditionally sought to avoid domination by the more powerful nations which surround it through a policy of mediation. The Belgians have been strong advocates of <a href="/wiki/European_integration" title="European integration">European integration</a>. Both the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> and <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a> are headquartered in Belgium.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Armed_forces">Armed forces</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Belgian_Armed_Forces" title="Belgian Armed Forces">Belgian Armed Forces</a></div>
<p>The Belgian Armed Forces have about 47,000 active troops. In 2010, Belgium's defense budget totaled €3.95&#160;billion (representing 1.12% of its GDP).<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> They are organized into one unified structure which consists of four main components: <a href="/wiki/Belgian_Land_Component" title="Belgian Land Component">Land Component</a>, or the Army; <a href="/wiki/Belgian_Air_Component" title="Belgian Air Component">Air Component</a>, or the Air Force; <a href="/wiki/Belgian_Naval_Component" class="mw-redirect" title="Belgian Naval Component">Naval Component</a>, or the Navy; <a href="/wiki/Belgian_Medical_Component" title="Belgian Medical Component">Medical Component</a>. The operational commands of the four components are subordinate to the Staff Department for Operations and Training of the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Defence_(Belgium)" title="Ministry of Defence (Belgium)">Ministry of Defense</a>, which is headed by the <a href="/wiki/ACOS_Operations_and_Training" class="mw-redirect" title="ACOS Operations and Training">Assistant Chief of Staff Operations and Training</a>, and to the <a href="/wiki/Chief_of_Defence_(Belgium)" title="Chief of Defence (Belgium)">Chief of Defense</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The effects of the <a href="/wiki/Second_World_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Second World War">Second World War</a> made <a href="/wiki/Collective_security" title="Collective security">collective security</a> a priority for <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Belgium" title="Foreign relations of Belgium">Belgian foreign policy</a>. In March 1948 Belgium signed the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Brussels" title="Treaty of Brussels">Treaty of Brussels</a> and then joined <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a> in 1948. However, the integration of the armed forces into NATO did not begin until after the <a href="/wiki/Korean_War" title="Korean War">Korean War</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> The Belgians, along with the Luxembourg government, sent a detachment of battalion strength to fight in Korea known as the <a href="/wiki/Belgian_United_Nations_Command" title="Belgian United Nations Command">Belgian United Nations Command</a>. This mission was the first in a long line of UN missions which the Belgians supported. Currently, the Belgian Naval Component is working closely together with the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Navy" class="mw-redirect" title="Dutch Navy">Dutch Navy</a> under the command of the <a href="/wiki/Admiral_Benelux" title="Admiral Benelux">Admiral Benelux</a>.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Belgium" title="Economy of Belgium">Economy of Belgium</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:BlueEurozone_2019.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/BlueEurozone_2019.svg/220px-BlueEurozone_2019.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="235" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/BlueEurozone_2019.svg/330px-BlueEurozone_2019.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/BlueEurozone_2019.svg/440px-BlueEurozone_2019.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="645" data-file-height="690" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:BlueEurozone_2019.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Belgium is part of a monetary union, the <a href="/wiki/Eurozone" title="Eurozone">eurozone</a> (dark blue), and of the <a href="/wiki/Internal_Market_(European_Union)" class="mw-redirect" title="Internal Market (European Union)">EU single market</a></div></div></div>
<p>Belgium's strongly globalized economy<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> and its <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Belgium" title="Transport in Belgium">transport infrastructure</a> are integrated with the rest of Europe. Its location at the heart of a highly industrialized region helped make it the world's 15th largest trading nation in 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> The economy is characterized by a highly productive work force, high <a href="/wiki/Gross_national_product" class="mw-redirect" title="Gross national product">GNP</a> and high exports per capita.<sup id="cite_ref-diplomatbe1_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-diplomatbe1-95">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> Belgium's main imports are raw materials, machinery and equipment, chemicals, raw diamonds, pharmaceuticals, foodstuffs, transportation equipment, and oil products. Its main exports are machinery and equipment, chemicals, finished diamonds, metals and metal products, and foodstuffs.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_38-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-38">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Belgian economy is heavily service-oriented and shows a dual nature: a dynamic Flemish economy and a Walloon economy that lags behind.<sup id="cite_ref-Fitzmaurice_13-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fitzmaurice-13">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;D&#93;</a></sup> One of the founding members of the European Union, Belgium strongly supports an <a href="/wiki/Open_economy" title="Open economy">open economy</a> and the extension of the powers of EU institutions to integrate member economies. Since 1922, through the <a href="/wiki/Belgium-Luxembourg_Economic_Union" class="mw-redirect" title="Belgium-Luxembourg Economic Union">Belgium-Luxembourg Economic Union</a>, Belgium and Luxembourg have been a single trade market with customs and currency union.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ougr%C3%A9e_Cokerie.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Ougr%C3%A9e_Cokerie.jpg/220px-Ougr%C3%A9e_Cokerie.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Ougr%C3%A9e_Cokerie.jpg/330px-Ougr%C3%A9e_Cokerie.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Ougr%C3%A9e_Cokerie.jpg/440px-Ougr%C3%A9e_Cokerie.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ougr%C3%A9e_Cokerie.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Steelmaking along the <a href="/wiki/Meuse_River" class="mw-redirect" title="Meuse River">Meuse River</a> at <a href="/wiki/Ougr%C3%A9e" title="Ougrée">Ougrée</a>, near <a href="/wiki/Li%C3%A8ge_(city)" class="mw-redirect" title="Liège (city)">Liège</a></div></div></div>
<p>Belgium was the first continental European country to undergo the <a href="/wiki/Industrial_Revolution" title="Industrial Revolution">Industrial Revolution</a>, in the early 19th century.<sup id="cite_ref-erih_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-erih-99">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Li%C3%A8ge_(city)" class="mw-redirect" title="Liège (city)">Liège</a> and <a href="/wiki/Charleroi" title="Charleroi">Charleroi</a> rapidly developed mining and steelmaking, which flourished until the mid-20th century in the <a href="/wiki/Sillon_industriel" title="Sillon industriel">Sambre and Meuse valley</a> and made Belgium among one of the three most industrialized nations in the world from 1830 to 1910.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup> However, by the 1840s the textile industry of Flanders was in severe crisis, and the region experienced <a href="/wiki/European_Potato_Failure" title="European Potato Failure">famine</a> from 1846 to 1850.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>After <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ghent" title="Ghent">Ghent</a> and <a href="/wiki/Antwerp" title="Antwerp">Antwerp</a> experienced a rapid expansion of the chemical and petroleum industries. The <a href="/wiki/1973_oil_crisis" title="1973 oil crisis">1973</a> and <a href="/wiki/1979_oil_crisis" title="1979 oil crisis">1979 oil crises</a> sent the economy into a recession; it was particularly prolonged in Wallonia, where the steel industry had become less competitive and experienced a serious decline.<sup id="cite_ref-usdepartmentofstate1_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-usdepartmentofstate1-104">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> In the 1980s and 1990s, the economic center of the country continued to shift northwards and is now concentrated in the populous <a href="/wiki/Flemish_Diamond" title="Flemish Diamond">Flemish Diamond</a> area.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>By the end of the 1980s, Belgian <a href="/wiki/Macroeconomic_policies" class="mw-redirect" title="Macroeconomic policies">macroeconomic policies</a> had resulted in a cumulative government debt of about 120% of GDP. As of 2006<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Belgium&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, the budget was balanced and public debt was equal to 90.30% of GDP.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> In 2005 and 2006, real GDP growth rates of 1.5% and 3.0%, respectively, were slightly above the average for the Euro area. Unemployment rates of 8.4% in 2005 and 8.2% in 2006 were close to the area average. By <span class="nowrap">October 2010</span>, this had grown to 8.5% compared to an average rate of 9.6% for the European Union as a whole (EU 27).<sup id="cite_ref-nbb_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nbb-107">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> From 1832 until 2002, Belgium's currency was the <a href="/wiki/Belgian_franc" title="Belgian franc">Belgian franc</a>. Belgium switched to the euro in 2002, with the first sets of euro coins being minted in 1999. The standard <a href="/wiki/Belgian_euro_coins" title="Belgian euro coins">Belgian euro coins</a> designated for circulation show the portrait of the monarch (first King Albert&#160;II, since 2013 King Philippe).
</p><p>Despite an 18% decrease observed from 1970 to 1999, Belgium still had in 1999 the highest <a href="/wiki/Rail_transport_in_Belgium" title="Rail transport in Belgium">rail network</a> density within the European Union with 113.8&#160;km/1 000&#160;km<sup>2</sup>. On the other hand, the same period, 1970–1999, has seen a huge growth (+56%) of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_motorways_in_Belgium" title="List of motorways in Belgium">motorway network</a>. In 1999, the density of km motorways per 1000&#160;km<sup>2</sup> and 1000 inhabitants amounted to 55.1 and 16.5 respectively and were significantly superior to the EU's means of 13.7 and 15.9.<sup id="cite_ref-panorama_109-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-panorama-109">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Port_cranes_at_Zeebr%C3%BCgge,_Belgium_2.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Port_cranes_at_Zeebr%C3%BCgge%2C_Belgium_2.JPG/220px-Port_cranes_at_Zeebr%C3%BCgge%2C_Belgium_2.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Port_cranes_at_Zeebr%C3%BCgge%2C_Belgium_2.JPG/330px-Port_cranes_at_Zeebr%C3%BCgge%2C_Belgium_2.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Port_cranes_at_Zeebr%C3%BCgge%2C_Belgium_2.JPG/440px-Port_cranes_at_Zeebr%C3%BCgge%2C_Belgium_2.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="1944" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Port_cranes_at_Zeebr%C3%BCgge,_Belgium_2.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Port_of_Zeebrugge" title="Port of Zeebrugge">Port of Zeebrugge</a></div></div></div>
<p>Belgium experiences some of the most congested traffic in Europe. In 2010, commuters to the cities of Brussels and Antwerp spent respectively 65 and 64 hours a year in traffic jams.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup> Like in most small European countries, more than 80% of the airways traffic is handled by a single airport, the <a href="/wiki/Brussels_Airport" title="Brussels Airport">Brussels Airport</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Antwerp" title="Port of Antwerp">ports of Antwerp</a> and <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Zeebrugge" title="Port of Zeebrugge">Zeebrugge (Bruges)</a> share more than 80% of Belgian maritime traffic, Antwerp being the second European harbor with a gross weight of goods handled of 115 988 000 t in 2000 after a growth of 10.9% over the preceding five years.<sup id="cite_ref-panorama_109-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-panorama-109">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup> In 2016, the port of Antwerp handled 214 million tons after a year-on-year growth of 2.7%.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>There is a large economic gap between <a href="/wiki/Flanders" title="Flanders">Flanders</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wallonia" title="Wallonia">Wallonia</a>. Wallonia was historically wealthy compared to Flanders, mostly due to its <a href="/wiki/Heavy_industry" title="Heavy industry">heavy industries</a>, but the decline of the steel industry post-World War II led to the region's rapid decline, whereas Flanders rose swiftly. Since then, Flanders has been prosperous, among the wealthiest regions in Europe, whereas Wallonia has been languishing. As of 2007, the unemployment rate of Wallonia is over double that of Flanders. The divide has played a key part in the tensions between the Flemish and Walloons in addition to the already-existing language divide. <a href="/wiki/Flemish_Movement" title="Flemish Movement">Pro-independence movements</a> have gained high popularity in Flanders as a consequence. The separatist <a href="/wiki/New_Flemish_Alliance" title="New Flemish Alliance">New Flemish Alliance</a> (N-VA) party, for instance, is the largest party in Belgium.<sup id="cite_ref-Crisis_113-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Crisis-113">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Divided_114-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Divided-114">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-google_115-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-google-115">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Science_and_technology">Science and technology</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Science_and_technology_in_Brussels" title="Science and technology in Brussels">Science and technology in Brussels</a>, <a href="/wiki/Science_and_technology_in_Flanders" title="Science and technology in Flanders">Science and technology in Flanders</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Science_and_technology_in_Wallonia" title="Science and technology in Wallonia">Science and technology in Wallonia</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mercator.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Mercator.jpg/170px-Mercator.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="235" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Mercator.jpg/255px-Mercator.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Mercator.jpg/340px-Mercator.jpg 2x" data-file-width="540" data-file-height="746" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Mercator.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Gerardus_Mercator" title="Gerardus Mercator">Gerardus Mercator</a></div></div></div>
<p>Contributions to the development of science and technology have appeared throughout the country's history. The 16th century <a href="/wiki/Early_Modern" class="mw-redirect" title="Early Modern">Early Modern</a> flourishing of Western Europe included <a href="/wiki/Cartography" title="Cartography">cartographer</a> <a href="/wiki/Gerardus_Mercator" title="Gerardus Mercator">Gerardus Mercator</a>, <a href="/wiki/Anatomy" title="Anatomy">anatomist</a> <a href="/wiki/Andreas_Vesalius" title="Andreas Vesalius">Andreas Vesalius</a>, <a href="/wiki/Herbalist" class="mw-redirect" title="Herbalist">herbalist</a> <a href="/wiki/Rembert_Dodoens" title="Rembert Dodoens">Rembert Dodoens</a><sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Mathematics" title="Mathematics">mathematician</a> <a href="/wiki/Simon_Stevin" title="Simon Stevin">Simon Stevin</a> among the most influential scientists.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Chemist <a href="/wiki/Ernest_Solvay" title="Ernest Solvay">Ernest Solvay</a><sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> and engineer <a href="/wiki/Zenobe_Gramme" class="mw-redirect" title="Zenobe Gramme">Zenobe Gramme</a> (École industrielle de Liège)<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup> gave their names to the <a href="/wiki/Solvay_process" title="Solvay process">Solvay process</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Gramme_dynamo" class="mw-redirect" title="Gramme dynamo">Gramme dynamo</a>, respectively, in the 1860s. <a href="/wiki/Bakelite" title="Bakelite">Bakelite</a> was developed in 1907–1909 by <a href="/wiki/Leo_Baekeland" title="Leo Baekeland">Leo Baekeland</a>. Ernest Solvay also acted as a major philanthropist and gave its name to the <a href="/wiki/Solvay_Institute_of_Sociology" title="Solvay Institute of Sociology">Solvay Institute of Sociology</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Solvay_Brussels_School_of_Economics_and_Management" title="Solvay Brussels School of Economics and Management">Solvay Brussels School of Economics and Management</a> and the International Solvay Institutes for Physics and Chemistry which are now part of the <a href="/wiki/Universit%C3%A9_libre_de_Bruxelles" title="Université libre de Bruxelles">Université libre de Bruxelles</a>. In 1911, he started a series of conferences, the <a href="/wiki/Solvay_Conference" title="Solvay Conference">Solvay Conferences</a> on Physics and Chemistry, which have had a deep impact on the evolution of quantum physics and chemistry.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup> A major contribution to fundamental science was also due to a Belgian, <a href="/wiki/Monsignor" title="Monsignor">Monsignor</a> <a href="/wiki/Georges_Lema%C3%AEtre" title="Georges Lemaître">Georges Lemaître</a> (<a href="/wiki/Catholic_University_of_Leuven_(1834%E2%80%931968)" title="Catholic University of Leuven (1834–1968)">Catholic University of Louvain</a>), who is credited with proposing the <a href="/wiki/Big_Bang" title="Big Bang">Big Bang</a> theory of the origin of the universe in 1927.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Three <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Physiology_or_Medicine" title="Nobel Prize in Physiology or Medicine">Nobel Prizes in Physiology or Medicine</a> were awarded to Belgians: <a href="/wiki/Jules_Bordet" title="Jules Bordet">Jules Bordet</a> (Université libre de Bruxelles) in 1919, <a href="/wiki/Corneille_Heymans" title="Corneille Heymans">Corneille Heymans</a> (<a href="/wiki/University_of_Ghent" class="mw-redirect" title="University of Ghent">University of Ghent</a>) in 1938 and <a href="/wiki/Albert_Claude" title="Albert Claude">Albert Claude</a> (Université libre de Bruxelles) together with <a href="/wiki/Christian_de_Duve" title="Christian de Duve">Christian de Duve</a> (<a href="/wiki/Universit%C3%A9_catholique_de_Louvain" title="Université catholique de Louvain">Université catholique de Louvain</a>) in 1974. <a href="/wiki/Fran%C3%A7ois_Englert" title="François Englert">François Englert</a> (Université libre de Bruxelles) was awarded the <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Physics" title="Nobel Prize in Physics">Nobel Prize in Physics</a> in 2013. <a href="/wiki/Ilya_Prigogine" title="Ilya Prigogine">Ilya Prigogine</a> (Université libre de Bruxelles) was awarded the <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Chemistry" title="Nobel Prize in Chemistry">Nobel Prize in Chemistry</a> in 1977.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup> Two Belgian mathematicians have been awarded the <a href="/wiki/Fields_Medal" title="Fields Medal">Fields Medal</a>: <a href="/wiki/Pierre_Deligne" title="Pierre Deligne">Pierre Deligne</a> in 1978 and <a href="/wiki/Jean_Bourgain" title="Jean Bourgain">Jean Bourgain</a> in 1994.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Belgium" title="Demographics of Belgium">Demographics of Belgium</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:00_Bruxelles_-_Mont_des_Arts.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/00_Bruxelles_-_Mont_des_Arts.jpg/220px-00_Bruxelles_-_Mont_des_Arts.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="164" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/00_Bruxelles_-_Mont_des_Arts.jpg/330px-00_Bruxelles_-_Mont_des_Arts.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/00_Bruxelles_-_Mont_des_Arts.jpg/440px-00_Bruxelles_-_Mont_des_Arts.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2225" data-file-height="1654" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:00_Bruxelles_-_Mont_des_Arts.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Brussels" title="Brussels">Brussels</a>, the capital city and largest metropolitan area of Belgium</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:HM_Queen_Paola,_Princess_of_Belgium.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/HM_Queen_Paola%2C_Princess_of_Belgium.jpg/170px-HM_Queen_Paola%2C_Princess_of_Belgium.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="228" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/HM_Queen_Paola%2C_Princess_of_Belgium.jpg/255px-HM_Queen_Paola%2C_Princess_of_Belgium.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/HM_Queen_Paola%2C_Princess_of_Belgium.jpg/340px-HM_Queen_Paola%2C_Princess_of_Belgium.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1921" data-file-height="2581" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:HM_Queen_Paola,_Princess_of_Belgium.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Queen_Paola_of_Belgium" title="Queen Paola of Belgium">Queen Paola</a>, born and raised in <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a>, is of <a href="/wiki/Italians" title="Italians">Italian</a> and Belgian ancestry.</div></div></div>
<p>As of 1&#160;January&#160;2018<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Belgium&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, the total population of Belgium according to its population register was 11,376,070.<sup id="cite_ref-Population_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Population-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> Almost all of the population is urban, at 97% in 2004.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup> The population density of Belgium is 373 per square kilometre (966 per square mile) as of January&#160;2018<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Belgium&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>. The most densely inhabited area is Flanders.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup> The Ardennes have the lowest density. As of 1&#160;January&#160;2018<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Belgium&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, the Flemish Region had a population of 6,552,967, its most populous cities being <a href="/wiki/Antwerp" title="Antwerp">Antwerp</a> (523,248), Ghent (260,341) and <a href="/wiki/Bruges" title="Bruges">Bruges</a> (118,284). Wallonia had 3,624,377 with <a href="/wiki/Charleroi" title="Charleroi">Charleroi</a> (201,816), <a href="/wiki/Li%C3%A8ge" title="Liège">Liège</a> (197,355) and <a href="/wiki/Namur_(city)" class="mw-redirect" title="Namur (city)">Namur</a> (110,939), its most populous cities. <a href="/wiki/Brussels" title="Brussels">Brussels</a> has 1,198,726 inhabitants in the Capital Region's <a href="/wiki/List_of_municipalities_of_the_Brussels-Capital_Region" title="List of municipalities of the Brussels-Capital Region">19 municipalities</a>, three of which have over 100,000 residents.<sup id="cite_ref-Population_3-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Population-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2017 the average <a href="/wiki/Total_fertility_rate" title="Total fertility rate">total fertility rate</a> (TFR) across Belgium was 1.64 children per woman, below the replacement rate of 2.1, it remains considerably below the high of 4.87 children born per woman in 1873.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup> Belgium subsequently has one of the oldest populations in the world, with the average age of 41.5 years.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Migration">Migration</span></h3>
<table class="box-Update plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Update" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><img alt="Ambox current red.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/42px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png" decoding="async" width="42" height="34" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/63px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/84px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="360" data-file-height="290" /></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section needs to be <b>updated</b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please update this article to reflect recent events or newly available information.</span>  <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">June 2017</span>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>As of 2007<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Belgium&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, nearly 92% of the population had Belgian citizenship,<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup> and other European Union member citizens account for around 6%. The prevalent foreign nationals were Italian (171,918), French (125,061), Dutch (116,970), <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">Moroccan</a> (80,579), <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_people" title="Portuguese people">Portuguese</a> (43,509), Spanish (42,765), <a href="/wiki/Turkish_people" title="Turkish people">Turkish</a> (39,419) and German (37,621).<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup> In 2007, there were 1.38&#160;million foreign-born residents in Belgium, corresponding to 12.9% of the total population. Of these, 685,000 (6.4%) were born outside the EU and 695,000 (6.5%) were born in another EU Member State.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>At the beginning of 2012, people of foreign background and their descendants were estimated to have formed around 25% of the total population i.e. 2.8&#160;million <i>new Belgians</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-npdata.be_137-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-npdata.be-137">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup> Of these new Belgians, 1,200,000 are of European ancestry and 1,350,000<sup id="cite_ref-npdata_138-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-npdata-138">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup> are from non-Western countries (most of them from <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">Morocco</a>, <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Democratic Republic of the Congo">DR Congo</a>). Since the modification of the <a href="/wiki/Belgian_nationality_law" title="Belgian nationality law">Belgian nationality law</a> in 1984 more than <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Belgium" title="Demographics of Belgium">1.3&#160;million migrants have acquired Belgian citizenship</a>. The largest group of immigrants and their descendants in Belgium are <a href="/wiki/Moroccan_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Moroccan people">Moroccans</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-hbvl.be_139-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hbvl.be-139">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup> 89.2% of inhabitants of <a href="/wiki/Turkish_people" title="Turkish people">Turkish</a> origin have been naturalized, as have 88.4% of people of Moroccan background, 75.4% of Italians, 56.2% of the French and 47.8% of Dutch people.<sup id="cite_ref-npdata_138-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-npdata-138">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><br />
</p>

<td style="text-align:left;"><a href="/wiki/Antwerp" title="Antwerp">Antwerp</a></td>
<td style="text-align:left;"><a href="/wiki/Flanders" title="Flanders">Flanders</a></td>
<td style="text-align:right;">523,248</td>
<td style="text-align:center;background:#f0f0f0;">11</td>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Belgium" title="Languages of Belgium">Languages of Belgium</a></div>
<div class="barbox tright" style="overflow-x: auto;">
<div style="border:1px solid silver; font-size:88%; padding:0.4em; width:auto; background: white;">
<table style="text-align:left; border-collapse:collapse; width:100%;">

<td style="padding:0 4px; text-align:left;"></td>
