</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Brussels_signs.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Brussels_signs.jpg/220px-Brussels_signs.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Brussels_signs.jpg/330px-Brussels_signs.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Brussels_signs.jpg/440px-Brussels_signs.jpg 2x" data-file-width="552" data-file-height="368" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Brussels_signs.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Bilingual" class="mw-redirect" title="Bilingual">Bilingual</a> signs in Brussels</div></div></div>
<p>Belgium has three official languages: Dutch, French and German. A number of non-official minority languages are spoken as well.<sup id="cite_ref-Ethnologue-16thEd_141-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ethnologue-16thEd-141">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup>
As no census exists, there are no official statistical data regarding the distribution or usage of Belgium's three official languages or their <a href="/wiki/Dialect" title="Dialect">dialects</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup> However, various criteria, including the language(s) of parents, of education, or the second-language status of foreign born, may provide suggested figures. An estimated 60% of the Belgian population are native speakers of Dutch (often referred to as Flemish), and 40% of the population speaks French natively. French-speaking Belgians are often referred to as Walloons, although the French speakers in Brussels are not Walloons.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">&#91;E&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The total number of native Dutch speakers is estimated to be about 6.23&#160;million, concentrated in the northern Flanders region, while native French speakers number 3.32&#160;million in Wallonia and an estimated 870,000 (or 85%) in the officially bilingual Brussels-Capital Region.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">&#91;F&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-britishcouncil_145-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-britishcouncil-145">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/German-speaking_Community_of_Belgium" title="German-speaking Community of Belgium">German-speaking Community</a> is made up of 73,000 people in the east of the <a href="/wiki/Wallonia" title="Wallonia">Walloon Region</a>; around 10,000 German and 60,000 Belgian nationals are speakers of German. Roughly 23,000 more German speakers live in municipalities near the official Community.<sup id="cite_ref-German-speaking_Community_146-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-German-speaking_Community-146">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Both <a href="/wiki/Belgian_Dutch" class="mw-redirect" title="Belgian Dutch">Belgian Dutch</a> and <a href="/wiki/Belgian_French" title="Belgian French">Belgian French</a> have <a href="/wiki/Cognate" title="Cognate">minor differences</a> in vocabulary and semantic nuances from the varieties spoken respectively in the Netherlands and France. Many Flemish people still speak <a href="/wiki/Dutch_dialects" title="Dutch dialects">dialects of Dutch</a> in their local environment. <a href="/wiki/Walloon_language" title="Walloon language">Walloon</a>, considered either as a dialect of French or a distinct <a href="/wiki/Romance_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Romance language">Romance language</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup> is now only understood and spoken occasionally, mostly by elderly people. Walloon is divided into four dialects, which along with those of <a href="/wiki/Picard_language" title="Picard language">Picard</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Ethnologue-15thEd_152-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ethnologue-15thEd-152">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup> are rarely used in public life and have largely been replaced by French.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Belgium" title="Religion in Belgium">Religion in Belgium</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:242px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Basilica_of_the_Sacred_Heart-2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Basilica_of_the_Sacred_Heart-2.jpg/240px-Basilica_of_the_Sacred_Heart-2.jpg" decoding="async" width="240" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Basilica_of_the_Sacred_Heart-2.jpg/360px-Basilica_of_the_Sacred_Heart-2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Basilica_of_the_Sacred_Heart-2.jpg/480px-Basilica_of_the_Sacred_Heart-2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3558" data-file-height="2445" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Basilica_of_the_Sacred_Heart-2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Basilica_of_the_Sacred_Heart,_Brussels" title="Basilica of the Sacred Heart, Brussels">National Basilica of the Sacred Heart</a> in <a href="/wiki/Koekelberg" title="Koekelberg">Koekelberg</a>, Brussels</div></div></div>
<p>Since the country's independence, <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholicism" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholicism">Roman Catholicism</a>, counterbalanced by strong <a href="/wiki/Freethought" title="Freethought">freethought</a> movements, has had an important role in Belgium's politics.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup> However Belgium is largely a secular country as the <i><a href="/wiki/Laicite" class="mw-redirect" title="Laicite">laicist</a></i> <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Belgium" title="Constitution of Belgium">constitution</a> provides for freedom of religion, and the government generally respects this right in practice. During the reigns of <a href="/wiki/Albert_I_of_Belgium" title="Albert I of Belgium">Albert&#160;I</a> and <a href="/wiki/Baudouin_I_of_Belgium" class="mw-redirect" title="Baudouin I of Belgium">Baudouin</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Belgian_royal_family" class="mw-redirect" title="Belgian royal family">Belgian royal family</a> had a reputation of deeply rooted Catholicism.<sup id="cite_ref-MarshallCavendish2009_154-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MarshallCavendish2009-154">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Roman Catholicism has traditionally been Belgium's majority religion; being especially strong in Flanders. However, by 2009 Sunday <a href="/wiki/Church_attendance" title="Church attendance">church attendance</a> was 5% for Belgium in total; 3% in Brussels,<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup> and 5.4% in Flanders. Church attendance in 2009 in Belgium was roughly half of the Sunday church attendance in 1998 (11% for the total of Belgium in 1998).<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup> Despite the drop in church attendance, Catholic identity nevertheless remains an important part of Belgium's culture.<sup id="cite_ref-MarshallCavendish2009_154-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MarshallCavendish2009-154">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>According to the Eurobarometer 2010,<sup id="cite_ref-Special_Eurobarometer_393_157-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Special_Eurobarometer_393-157">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup> 37% of Belgian citizens responded that they believe there is a God. 31% answered that they believe there is some sort of spirit or life-force. 27% answered that they do not believe there is any sort of spirit, God, or life-force. 5% did not respond. According to the Eurobarometer 2015, 60.7% of the total population of Belgium adhered to Christianity, with Roman Catholicism being the largest denomination with 52.9%. Protestants comprised 2.1% and Orthodox Christians were the 1.6% of the total. Non-religious people comprised the 32.0% of the population and were divided between atheists (14.9%) and agnostics (17.1%). A further 5.2% of the population was Muslim and 2.1% were believers in other religions.<sup id="cite_ref-EB2015_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EB2015-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> The same survey held in 2012 found that Christianity was the largest religion in Belgium accounting 65% of <a href="/wiki/Belgians" title="Belgians">Belgians</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-EUROBAROMETER_158-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EUROBAROMETER-158">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Symbolically and materially, the Roman Catholic Church remains in a favorable position.<sup id="cite_ref-MarshallCavendish2009_154-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MarshallCavendish2009-154">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup> Belgium officially recognizes three religions: Christianity (Catholic, Protestantism, Orthodox churches and Anglicanism), Islam and Judaism.<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Syna_Bruxelles-2.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Syna_Bruxelles-2.JPG/150px-Syna_Bruxelles-2.JPG" decoding="async" width="150" height="200" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Syna_Bruxelles-2.JPG/225px-Syna_Bruxelles-2.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Syna_Bruxelles-2.JPG/300px-Syna_Bruxelles-2.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1536" data-file-height="2048" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Syna_Bruxelles-2.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Interior of the <a href="/wiki/Great_Synagogue_of_Brussels" class="mw-redirect" title="Great Synagogue of Brussels">Great Synagogue of Brussels</a></div></div></div>
<p>In the early 2000s, there were approximately 42,000 Jews in Belgium. The <a href="/wiki/Jewish_Community_of_Antwerp" class="mw-redirect" title="Jewish Community of Antwerp">Jewish Community of Antwerp</a> (numbering some 18,000) is one of the largest in Europe, and one of the last places in the world where <a href="/wiki/Yiddish" title="Yiddish">Yiddish</a> is the primary language of a large Jewish community (mirroring certain Orthodox and Hasidic communities in New York, New Jersey, and Israel). In addition, most Jewish children in Antwerp receive a Jewish education.<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup> There are several Jewish newspapers and more than 45 active synagogues (30 of which are in Antwerp) in the country.
A 2006 inquiry in Flanders, considered to be a more religious region than Wallonia, showed that 55% considered themselves religious and that 36% believed that God created the universe.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup> On the other hand, Wallonia has become one of Europe's most secular/least religious regions. Most of the French-speaking region's population does not consider religion an important part of their lives, and as much as 45% of the population identifies as irreligious. This is particularly the case in eastern Wallonia and areas along the French border.
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Brussel_052_Jubelpark.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Brussel_052_Jubelpark.JPG/200px-Brussel_052_Jubelpark.JPG" decoding="async" width="200" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Brussel_052_Jubelpark.JPG/300px-Brussel_052_Jubelpark.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Brussel_052_Jubelpark.JPG/400px-Brussel_052_Jubelpark.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Brussel_052_Jubelpark.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Great_Mosque_of_Brussels" title="Great Mosque of Brussels">Great Mosque of Brussels</a> is the seat of the <i>Islamic and Cultural Center of Belgium</i></div></div></div>
<p>A 2008 estimate found that approximately 6% of the Belgian population (628,751 people) is <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Belgium" title="Islam in Belgium">Muslim</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup> Muslims constitute 23.6% of the population of <a href="/wiki/Brussels" title="Brussels">Brussels</a>, 4.9% of <a href="/wiki/Wallonia" title="Wallonia">Wallonia</a> and 5.1% of <a href="/wiki/Flanders" title="Flanders">Flanders</a>. The majority of Belgian Muslims live in the major cities, such as <a href="/wiki/Antwerp" title="Antwerp">Antwerp</a>, Brussels and <a href="/wiki/Charleroi" title="Charleroi">Charleroi</a>. The largest group of immigrants in Belgium are Moroccans, with 400,000 people. The Turks are the third largest group, and the second largest Muslim ethnic group, numbering 220,000.<sup id="cite_ref-hbvl.be_139-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hbvl.be-139">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Health">Health</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Healthcare_in_Belgium" title="Healthcare in Belgium">Healthcare in Belgium</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:UZA_ziekenhuis.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/UZA_ziekenhuis.jpg/220px-UZA_ziekenhuis.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="106" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/UZA_ziekenhuis.jpg/330px-UZA_ziekenhuis.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/UZA_ziekenhuis.jpg/440px-UZA_ziekenhuis.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="580" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:UZA_ziekenhuis.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>University Hospital of Antwerp</div></div></div>
<p>The Belgians enjoy good health. According to 2012 estimates, the average life expectancy is 79.65 years.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_38-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-38">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> Since 1960, life expectancy has, in line with the European average, grown by two months per year. Death in Belgium is mainly due to heart and vascular disorders, <a href="/wiki/Neoplasm" title="Neoplasm">neoplasms</a>, disorders of the respiratory system and unnatural causes of death (accidents, suicide). Non-natural causes of death and cancer are the most common causes of death for females up to age 24 and males up to age 44.<sup id="cite_ref-Corens2007_164-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Corens2007-164">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Healthcare_in_Belgium" title="Healthcare in Belgium">Healthcare in Belgium</a> is financed through both social security contributions and taxation. Health insurance is compulsory. Health care is delivered by a mixed public and private system of independent medical practitioners and public, university and semi-private hospitals. Health care service are payable by the patient and reimbursed later by health insurance institutions, but for ineligible categories (of patients and services) so-called 3rd party payment systems exist.<sup id="cite_ref-Corens2007_164-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Corens2007-164">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup> The Belgian health care system is supervised and financed by the federal government, the Flemish and Walloon Regional governments; and the German Community also has (indirect) oversight and responsibilities.<sup id="cite_ref-Corens2007_164-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Corens2007-164">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>For the first time in Belgian history, the first child was euthanized following the 2 year mark of the removal of the euthanization age restrictions. The child had been euthanized due to an incurable disease that was inflicted upon the child. Although there may have been some support for the euthanization there is a possibility of controversy due to the issue revolving around the subject of assisted suicide.<sup id="cite_ref-cnn_165-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cnn-165">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-scu_166-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-scu-166">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Belgium" title="Education in Belgium">Education in Belgium</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:2011-09-24_17.42_Leuven,_universiteitsbibliotheek_ceg74154_foto4.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/2011-09-24_17.42_Leuven%2C_universiteitsbibliotheek_ceg74154_foto4.jpg/220px-2011-09-24_17.42_Leuven%2C_universiteitsbibliotheek_ceg74154_foto4.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/2011-09-24_17.42_Leuven%2C_universiteitsbibliotheek_ceg74154_foto4.jpg/330px-2011-09-24_17.42_Leuven%2C_universiteitsbibliotheek_ceg74154_foto4.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/2011-09-24_17.42_Leuven%2C_universiteitsbibliotheek_ceg74154_foto4.jpg/440px-2011-09-24_17.42_Leuven%2C_universiteitsbibliotheek_ceg74154_foto4.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4416" data-file-height="3312" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:2011-09-24_17.42_Leuven,_universiteitsbibliotheek_ceg74154_foto4.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Central Library of the <a href="/wiki/KU_Leuven" title="KU Leuven">KU Leuven</a> University</div></div></div>
<p>Education is compulsory from 6 to 18 years of age for Belgians.<sup id="cite_ref-Hofman_Hofman_Gray_Daly_167-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hofman_Hofman_Gray_Daly-167">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup> Among <a href="/wiki/Organisation_for_Economic_Co-operation_and_Development" class="mw-redirect" title="Organisation for Economic Co-operation and Development">OECD</a> countries in 2002, Belgium had the third highest proportion of 18- to 21-year-olds enrolled in <a href="/wiki/Postsecondary_education" class="mw-redirect" title="Postsecondary education">postsecondary education</a>, at 42%.<sup id="cite_ref-NCES_Tbl-388_168-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NCES_Tbl-388-168">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup> Though an estimated 99% of the adult population is literate, concern is rising over <a href="/wiki/Functional_illiteracy" title="Functional illiteracy">functional illiteracy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Ethnologue-15thEd_152-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ethnologue-15thEd-152">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-UNDP_169-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNDP-169">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Programme_for_International_Student_Assessment" title="Programme for International Student Assessment">Programme for International Student Assessment</a> (PISA), coordinated by the OECD, currently ranks Belgium's education as the 19th best in the world, being significantly higher than the OECD average.<sup id="cite_ref-OECD_PISA-2006_170-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OECD_PISA-2006-170">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup> Education being organized separately by each, the Flemish Community scores noticeably above the French and German-speaking Communities.<sup id="cite_ref-De-Meyer_Pauly_Van-de-Poele_171-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-De-Meyer_Pauly_Van-de-Poele-171">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Mirroring the dual structure of the 19th-century Belgian political landscape, characterized by the <a href="/wiki/Liberal_Party_(Belgium)" title="Liberal Party (Belgium)">Liberal</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Party_(Belgium)" title="Catholic Party (Belgium)">Catholic parties</a>, the educational system is segregated within a secular and a religious segment. The secular branch of schooling is controlled by the communities, the provinces, or the municipalities, while religious, mainly <a href="/wiki/Catholic_school" title="Catholic school">Catholic branch</a> education, is organized by religious authorities, although subsidized and supervised by the communities.<sup id="cite_ref-De-Ley_172-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-De-Ley-172">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Belgium" title="Culture of Belgium">Culture of Belgium</a></div>
<p>Despite its <a href="/wiki/Partition_of_Belgium" title="Partition of Belgium">political and linguistic divisions</a>, the region corresponding to today's Belgium has seen the flourishing of major artistic movements that have had tremendous influence on European art and culture. Nowadays, to a certain extent, cultural life is concentrated within each language Community, and a variety of barriers have made a shared cultural sphere less pronounced.<sup id="cite_ref-Fitzmaurice_13-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fitzmaurice-13">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup> Since the 1970s, there are no bilingual universities or colleges in the country except the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Military_Academy_(Belgium)" title="Royal Military Academy (Belgium)">Royal Military Academy</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Antwerp_Maritime_Academy" title="Antwerp Maritime Academy">Antwerp Maritime Academy</a>, no common media<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup> and no single large cultural or scientific organization in which both main communities are represented.<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fine_arts">Fine arts</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Belgian_painters" title="List of Belgian painters">List of Belgian painters</a>, <a href="/wiki/Architecture_of_Belgium" class="mw-redirect" title="Architecture of Belgium">Architecture of Belgium</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Belgium" title="Music of Belgium">Music of Belgium</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Eyck.hubert.lamb.750pix.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Eyck.hubert.lamb.750pix.jpg/220px-Eyck.hubert.lamb.750pix.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="163" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Eyck.hubert.lamb.750pix.jpg/330px-Eyck.hubert.lamb.750pix.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Eyck.hubert.lamb.750pix.jpg/440px-Eyck.hubert.lamb.750pix.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1348" data-file-height="1000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Eyck.hubert.lamb.750pix.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i>The <a href="/wiki/Ghent_Altarpiece" title="Ghent Altarpiece">Ghent Altarpiece</a>: The Adoration of the Mystic Lamb</i> (interior view), painted 1432 by <a href="/wiki/Jan_van_Eyck" title="Jan van Eyck">van Eyck</a></div></div></div>
<p>Contributions to painting and architecture have been especially rich. The <a href="/wiki/Mosan_art" title="Mosan art">Mosan art</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Early_Netherlandish_painting" title="Early Netherlandish painting">Early Netherlandish</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_and_Flemish_Renaissance_painting" title="Dutch and Flemish Renaissance painting">Flemish Renaissance</a> and <a href="/wiki/Flemish_Baroque_painting" title="Flemish Baroque painting">Baroque painting</a><sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup> and major examples of <a href="/wiki/Romanesque_architecture" title="Romanesque architecture">Romanesque</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gothic_architecture" title="Gothic architecture">Gothic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Renaissance_architecture" title="Renaissance architecture">Renaissance</a> and <a href="/wiki/Baroque_architecture" title="Baroque architecture">Baroque architecture</a><sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup> are milestones in the history of art. While the 15th century's art in the Low Countries is dominated by the religious paintings of <a href="/wiki/Jan_van_Eyck" title="Jan van Eyck">Jan van Eyck</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rogier_van_der_Weyden" title="Rogier van der Weyden">Rogier van der Weyden</a>, the 16th century is characterized by a broader panel of styles such as <a href="/wiki/Pieter_Brueghel_the_Elder" class="mw-redirect" title="Pieter Brueghel the Elder">Peter Breughel</a>'s landscape paintings and <a href="/wiki/Lambert_Lombard" title="Lambert Lombard">Lambert Lombard</a>'s representation of the antique.<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup> Though the Baroque style of <a href="/wiki/Peter_Paul_Rubens" title="Peter Paul Rubens">Peter Paul Rubens</a> and <a href="/wiki/Anthony_van_Dyck" title="Anthony van Dyck">Anthony van Dyck</a> flourished in the early 17th century in the Southern Netherlands,<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup> it gradually declined thereafter.<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>During the 19th and 20th centuries many original <a href="/wiki/Romanticism" title="Romanticism">romantic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Expressionism" title="Expressionism">expressionist</a> and <a href="/wiki/Surrealism" title="Surrealism">surrealist</a> Belgian painters emerged, including <a href="/wiki/James_Ensor" title="James Ensor">James Ensor</a> and other artists belonging to the <a href="/wiki/Les_XX" title="Les XX">Les XX</a> group, <a href="/wiki/Constant_Permeke" title="Constant Permeke">Constant Permeke</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paul_Delvaux" title="Paul Delvaux">Paul Delvaux</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ren%C3%A9_Magritte" title="René Magritte">René Magritte</a>. The avant-garde <a href="/wiki/COBRA_(avant-garde_movement)" title="COBRA (avant-garde movement)">CoBrA movement</a> appeared in the 1950s, while the sculptor <a href="/wiki/Panamarenko" title="Panamarenko">Panamarenko</a> remains a remarkable figure in contemporary art.<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup> Multidisciplinary artists <a href="/wiki/Jan_Fabre" title="Jan Fabre">Jan Fabre</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wim_Delvoye" title="Wim Delvoye">Wim Delvoye</a> and the painter <a href="/wiki/Luc_Tuymans" title="Luc Tuymans">Luc Tuymans</a> are other internationally renowned figures on the contemporary art scene.
</p><p>Belgian contributions to architecture also continued into the 19th and 20th centuries, including the work of <a href="/wiki/Victor_Horta" title="Victor Horta">Victor Horta</a> and <a href="/wiki/Henry_van_de_Velde" title="Henry van de Velde">Henry van de Velde</a>, who were major initiators of the <a href="/wiki/Art_Nouveau" title="Art Nouveau">Art Nouveau</a> style.<sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:TV-uitzending_Domino_Jacques_Brel_tijdens_de_opname_in_Amsterdam,_Marcanti,_Bestanddeelnr_914-8399.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/TV-uitzending_Domino_Jacques_Brel_tijdens_de_opname_in_Amsterdam%2C_Marcanti%2C_Bestanddeelnr_914-8399.jpg/220px-TV-uitzending_Domino_Jacques_Brel_tijdens_de_opname_in_Amsterdam%2C_Marcanti%2C_Bestanddeelnr_914-8399.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="145" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/TV-uitzending_Domino_Jacques_Brel_tijdens_de_opname_in_Amsterdam%2C_Marcanti%2C_Bestanddeelnr_914-8399.jpg/330px-TV-uitzending_Domino_Jacques_Brel_tijdens_de_opname_in_Amsterdam%2C_Marcanti%2C_Bestanddeelnr_914-8399.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/TV-uitzending_Domino_Jacques_Brel_tijdens_de_opname_in_Amsterdam%2C_Marcanti%2C_Bestanddeelnr_914-8399.jpg/440px-TV-uitzending_Domino_Jacques_Brel_tijdens_de_opname_in_Amsterdam%2C_Marcanti%2C_Bestanddeelnr_914-8399.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3694" data-file-height="2434" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:TV-uitzending_Domino_Jacques_Brel_tijdens_de_opname_in_Amsterdam,_Marcanti,_Bestanddeelnr_914-8399.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Jacques_Brel" title="Jacques Brel">Jacques Brel</a>, 1963</div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Vocal_music" title="Vocal music">vocal music</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Franco-Flemish_School" title="Franco-Flemish School">Franco-Flemish School</a> developed in the southern part of the Low Countries and was an important contribution to Renaissance culture.<sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup> In the 19th and 20th centuries, there was an emergence of major violinists, such as <a href="/wiki/Henri_Vieuxtemps" title="Henri Vieuxtemps">Henri Vieuxtemps</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eug%C3%A8ne_Ysa%C3%BFe" title="Eugène Ysaÿe">Eugène Ysaÿe</a> and <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Grumiaux" title="Arthur Grumiaux">Arthur Grumiaux</a>, while <a href="/wiki/Adolphe_Sax" title="Adolphe Sax">Adolphe Sax</a> invented the saxophone in 1846. The composer <a href="/wiki/C%C3%A9sar_Franck" title="César Franck">César Franck</a> was born in Liège in 1822. Contemporary <a href="/wiki/Popular_music" title="Popular music">popular music</a> in Belgium is also of repute. Jazz musician <a href="/wiki/Toots_Thielemans" title="Toots Thielemans">Toots Thielemans</a> and singer <a href="/wiki/Jacques_Brel" title="Jacques Brel">Jacques Brel</a> have achieved global fame. Nowadays, singer <a href="/wiki/Stromae" title="Stromae">Stromae</a> has been a musical revelation in Europe and beyond, having great success. In rock/pop music, <a href="/wiki/Telex_(band)" title="Telex (band)">Telex</a>, <a href="/wiki/Front_242" title="Front 242">Front 242</a>, <a href="/wiki/K%27s_Choice" title="K&#39;s Choice">K's Choice</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hooverphonic" title="Hooverphonic">Hooverphonic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zap_Mama" title="Zap Mama">Zap Mama</a>, <a href="/wiki/Soulwax" title="Soulwax">Soulwax</a> and <a href="/wiki/Deus_(band)" title="Deus (band)">dEUS</a> are well known. In the heavy metal scene, bands like <a href="/wiki/Machiavel_(band)" title="Machiavel (band)">Machiavel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Channel_Zero_(band)" title="Channel Zero (band)">Channel Zero</a> and <a href="/wiki/Enthroned" title="Enthroned">Enthroned</a> have a worldwide fan-base.<sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">&#91;183&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Belgium has produced several well-known <a href="/wiki/Belgian_literature" title="Belgian literature">authors</a>, including the poets <a href="/wiki/Emile_Verhaeren" class="mw-redirect" title="Emile Verhaeren">Emile Verhaeren</a>, <a href="/wiki/Robert_Goffin" title="Robert Goffin">Robert Goffin</a> and novelists <a href="/wiki/Hendrik_Conscience" title="Hendrik Conscience">Hendrik Conscience</a>, <a href="/wiki/Georges_Simenon" title="Georges Simenon">Georges Simenon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Suzanne_Lilar" title="Suzanne Lilar">Suzanne Lilar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hugo_Claus" title="Hugo Claus">Hugo Claus</a> and <a href="/wiki/Am%C3%A9lie_Nothomb" title="Amélie Nothomb">Amélie Nothomb</a>. The poet and playwright <a href="/wiki/Maurice_Maeterlinck" title="Maurice Maeterlinck">Maurice Maeterlinck</a> won the <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_literature" class="mw-redirect" title="Nobel Prize in literature">Nobel Prize in literature</a> in 1911. <i><a href="/wiki/The_Adventures_of_Tintin" title="The Adventures of Tintin">The Adventures of Tintin</a></i> by <a href="/wiki/Herg%C3%A9" title="Hergé">Hergé</a> is the best known of <a href="/wiki/Franco-Belgian_comics" class="mw-redirect" title="Franco-Belgian comics">Franco-Belgian comics</a>, but many other major authors, including <a href="/wiki/Peyo" title="Peyo">Peyo</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/The_Smurfs" title="The Smurfs">The Smurfs</a></i>), <a href="/wiki/Andr%C3%A9_Franquin" title="André Franquin">André Franquin</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Gaston_Lagaffe" class="mw-redirect" title="Gaston Lagaffe">Gaston Lagaffe</a></i>), <a href="/wiki/Dupa" title="Dupa">Dupa</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Cubitus" title="Cubitus">Cubitus</a></i>), <a href="/wiki/Morris_(comics)" class="mw-redirect" title="Morris (comics)">Morris</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Lucky_Luke" title="Lucky Luke">Lucky Luke</a></i>), <a href="/wiki/Greg_(comics)" class="mw-redirect" title="Greg (comics)">Greg</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Achille_Talon" title="Achille Talon">Achille Talon</a></i>), <a href="/wiki/Lambil" title="Lambil">Lambil</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Les_Tuniques_Bleues" title="Les Tuniques Bleues">Les Tuniques Bleues</a></i>), <a href="/wiki/Edgar_P._Jacobs" title="Edgar P. Jacobs">Edgar P. Jacobs</a> and <a href="/wiki/Willy_Vandersteen" title="Willy Vandersteen">Willy Vandersteen</a> brought the Belgian cartoon strip industry a worldwide fame.<sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup> Additionally, famous crime author <a href="/wiki/Agatha_Christie" title="Agatha Christie">Agatha Christie</a> created the character <a href="/wiki/Hercule_Poirot" title="Hercule Poirot">Hercule Poirot</a>, a Belgian detective, who has served as a <a href="/wiki/Protagonist" title="Protagonist">protagonist</a> in a number of her acclaimed mystery novels.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Cinema_of_Belgium" title="Cinema of Belgium">Belgian cinema</a> has brought a number of mainly Flemish novels to life on-screen.<sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">&#91;G&#93;</a></sup> Other Belgian directors include <a href="/wiki/Andr%C3%A9_Delvaux" title="André Delvaux">André Delvaux</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stijn_Coninx" title="Stijn Coninx">Stijn Coninx</a>, <a href="/wiki/Luc_Dardenne" class="mw-redirect" title="Luc Dardenne">Luc</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jean-Pierre_Dardenne" class="mw-redirect" title="Jean-Pierre Dardenne">Jean-Pierre Dardenne</a>; well-known actors include <a href="/wiki/Jean-Claude_Van_Damme" title="Jean-Claude Van Damme">Jean-Claude Van Damme</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jan_Decleir" title="Jan Decleir">Jan Decleir</a> and <a href="/wiki/Marie_Gillain" title="Marie Gillain">Marie Gillain</a>; and successful films include <i><a href="/wiki/Bullhead_(film)" title="Bullhead (film)">Bullhead</a>, <a href="/wiki/Man_Bites_Dog_(film)" title="Man Bites Dog (film)">Man Bites Dog</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Alzheimer_Affair" class="mw-redirect" title="The Alzheimer Affair">The Alzheimer Affair</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">&#91;185&#93;</a></sup> In the 1980s, Antwerp's <a href="/wiki/Koninklijke_Academie_voor_Schone_Kunsten_Antwerpen" class="mw-redirect" title="Koninklijke Academie voor Schone Kunsten Antwerpen">Royal Academy of Fine Arts</a> produced important fashion trendsetters, known as the <a href="/wiki/Antwerp_Six" title="Antwerp Six">Antwerp Six</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">&#91;186&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Folklore">Folklore</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Folklore_of_Belgium" title="Folklore of Belgium">Folklore of Belgium</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Binche_-_Les_Gilles.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Binche_-_Les_Gilles.jpg/220px-Binche_-_Les_Gilles.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="157" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Binche_-_Les_Gilles.jpg/330px-Binche_-_Les_Gilles.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Binche_-_Les_Gilles.jpg/440px-Binche_-_Les_Gilles.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4056" data-file-height="2902" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Binche_-_Les_Gilles.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Gilles" title="Gilles">Gilles</a> of <a href="/wiki/Binche" title="Binche">Binche</a>, in costume, wearing wax masks</div></div></div>
<p>Folklore plays a major role in Belgium's cultural life: the country has a comparatively high number of processions, cavalcades, parades, 'ommegangs' and 'ducasses',<sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">&#91;H&#93;</a></sup> '<a href="/wiki/Kermesse_(festival)" title="Kermesse (festival)">kermesse</a>' and other local festivals, nearly always with an originally religious or <a href="/wiki/Mythology_of_the_Low_Countries" class="mw-redirect" title="Mythology of the Low Countries">mythological background</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Carnival_of_Binche" title="Carnival of Binche">Carnival of Binche</a> with its famous <a href="/wiki/Gilles" title="Gilles">Gilles</a> and the 'Processional Giants and Dragons' of <a href="/wiki/Ath" title="Ath">Ath</a>, Brussels, <a href="/wiki/Dendermonde" title="Dendermonde">Dendermonde</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mechelen" title="Mechelen">Mechelen</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mons" title="Mons">Mons</a> are recognized by <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> as <a href="/wiki/Masterpieces_of_the_Oral_and_Intangible_Heritage_of_Humanity" title="Masterpieces of the Oral and Intangible Heritage of Humanity">Masterpieces of the Oral and Intangible Heritage of Humanity</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195">&#91;187&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Other examples are the <a href="/wiki/Carnival_of_Aalst" title="Carnival of Aalst">Carnival of Aalst</a>; the still very religious processions of <a href="/wiki/Procession_of_the_Holy_Blood" title="Procession of the Holy Blood">the Holy Blood</a> in <a href="/wiki/Bruges" title="Bruges">Bruges</a>, <a href="/wiki/Virga_Jesse_Basilica" title="Virga Jesse Basilica">Virga Jesse Basilica</a> in <a href="/wiki/Hasselt" title="Hasselt">Hasselt</a> and <a href="/wiki/Basilica_of_Our_Lady_of_Hanswijk" title="Basilica of Our Lady of Hanswijk">Basilica of Our Lady of Hanswijk</a> in Mechelen; <span class="nowrap">15 August</span> festival in <a href="/wiki/Li%C3%A8ge" title="Liège">Liège</a>; and the Walloon festival in <a href="/wiki/Namur_(city)" class="mw-redirect" title="Namur (city)">Namur</a>. Originated in 1832 and revived in the 1960s, the <a href="/wiki/Gentse_Feesten" title="Gentse Feesten">Gentse Feesten</a> have become a modern tradition. A major non-official holiday is the <a href="/wiki/Saint_Nicholas_Day" title="Saint Nicholas Day">Saint Nicholas Day</a>, a festivity for children and, in Liège, for students.<sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">&#91;188&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Belgian_cuisine" title="Belgian cuisine">Belgian cuisine</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Moules_Frites.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Moules_Frites.jpg/220px-Moules_Frites.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Moules_Frites.jpg/330px-Moules_Frites.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Moules_Frites.jpg/440px-Moules_Frites.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="600" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Moules_Frites.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i><a href="/wiki/Moules-frites" title="Moules-frites">Moules-frites</a></i> / <i>mosselen met friet</i> is a representative dish of Belgium</div></div></div>
<p>Many highly ranked Belgian restaurants can be found in the most influential restaurant guides, such as the <a href="/wiki/Michelin_Guide" title="Michelin Guide">Michelin Guide</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">&#91;189&#93;</a></sup> Belgium is famous for <a href="/wiki/Beer" title="Beer">beer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chocolate" title="Chocolate">chocolate</a>, <a href="/wiki/Waffle" title="Waffle">waffles</a> and <a href="/wiki/French_fries" title="French fries">french fries</a> with <a href="/wiki/Mayonnaise" title="Mayonnaise">mayonnaise</a>. Contrary to their name, french fries are claimed to have originated in Belgium, although their exact place of origin is uncertain. The national dishes are "<a href="/wiki/Steak_frites" title="Steak frites">steak and fries</a> with salad", and "<a href="/wiki/Moules-frites" title="Moules-frites">mussels with fries</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198">&#91;190&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199">&#91;191&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200">&#91;192&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">&#91;I&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Brands of Belgian chocolate and <a href="/wiki/Pralines" class="mw-redirect" title="Pralines">pralines</a>, like <a href="/wiki/C%C3%B4te_d%27Or_(brand)" class="mw-redirect" title="Côte d&#39;Or (brand)">Côte d'Or</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chocolatier_Neuhaus" class="mw-redirect" title="Chocolatier Neuhaus">Neuhaus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Leonidas_(chocolate_maker)" title="Leonidas (chocolate maker)">Leonidas</a> and <a href="/wiki/Godiva_Chocolatier" title="Godiva Chocolatier">Godiva</a> are famous, as well as independent producers such as Burie and Del Rey in Antwerp and Mary's in Brussels.<sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">&#91;193&#93;</a></sup> Belgium produces over <a href="/wiki/Belgian_beer" class="mw-redirect" title="Belgian beer">1100 varieties of beer</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-BierbijbelNieuwsblad_203-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BierbijbelNieuwsblad-203">&#91;194&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BierbijbelKW_204-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BierbijbelKW-204">&#91;195&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Trappist_beer" title="Trappist beer">Trappist beer</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Westvleteren_Brewery" title="Westvleteren Brewery">Abbey of Westvleteren</a> has repeatedly been rated the world's best beer.<sup id="cite_ref-205" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-205">&#91;196&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-206" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-206">&#91;197&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207">&#91;198&#93;</a></sup>
The biggest brewer in the world by volume is <a href="/wiki/Anheuser-Busch_InBev" title="Anheuser-Busch InBev">Anheuser-Busch InBev</a>, based in <a href="/wiki/Leuven" title="Leuven">Leuven</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-208" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-208">&#91;199&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Eddy_Merckx_Molteni_1973.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Eddy_Merckx_Molteni_1973.jpg/170px-Eddy_Merckx_Molteni_1973.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="269" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Eddy_Merckx_Molteni_1973.jpg/255px-Eddy_Merckx_Molteni_1973.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Eddy_Merckx_Molteni_1973.jpg/340px-Eddy_Merckx_Molteni_1973.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1103" data-file-height="1748" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Eddy_Merckx_Molteni_1973.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Eddy_Merckx" title="Eddy Merckx">Eddy Merckx</a>, regarded as one of the greatest cyclists of all time</div></div></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sport_in_Belgium" title="Sport in Belgium">Sport in Belgium</a></div>
<p>Since the 1970s, sports clubs and federations are organized separately within each language community.<sup id="cite_ref-209" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-209">&#91;200&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">Association football</a> is the most popular sport in both parts of Belgium; also very popular are cycling, tennis, swimming, judo<sup id="cite_ref-210" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-210">&#91;201&#93;</a></sup> and basketball.<sup id="cite_ref-211" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-211">&#91;202&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Belgians hold <a href="/wiki/List_of_Tour_de_France_winners" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Tour de France winners">the most Tour de France victories</a> of any country except France. They have also the most victories on the <a href="/wiki/UCI_Road_World_Championships" title="UCI Road World Championships">UCI Road World Championships</a>. <a href="/wiki/Philippe_Gilbert" title="Philippe Gilbert">Philippe Gilbert</a> is the 2012 world champion. Another modern well-known Belgian cyclist is <a href="/wiki/Tom_Boonen" title="Tom Boonen">Tom Boonen</a>. With five victories in the <a href="/wiki/Tour_de_France" title="Tour de France">Tour de France</a> and numerous other cycling records, Belgian cyclist <a href="/wiki/Eddy_Merckx" title="Eddy Merckx">Eddy Merckx</a> is regarded as one of the greatest cyclists of all time.<sup id="cite_ref-212" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-212">&#91;203&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Jean-Marie_Pfaff" title="Jean-Marie Pfaff">Jean-Marie Pfaff</a>, a former Belgian goalkeeper, is considered one of the greatest in the history of association football.<sup id="cite_ref-213" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-213">&#91;204&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Belgium hosted the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_1972" title="UEFA Euro 1972">1972 European Football Championships</a>, and co-hosted the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2000" title="UEFA Euro 2000">2000 European Championships</a> with the Netherlands. The <a href="/wiki/Belgium_national_football_team" title="Belgium national football team">Belgium national football team</a> reached first place in the <a href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Rankings" title="FIFA World Rankings">FIFA World Rankings</a> for the first time in November 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-214" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-214">&#91;205&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Kim_Clijsters" title="Kim Clijsters">Kim Clijsters</a> and <a href="/wiki/Justine_Henin" title="Justine Henin">Justine Henin</a> both were <a href="/wiki/WTA_Awards" title="WTA Awards">Player of the Year</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Women%27s_Tennis_Association" title="Women&#39;s Tennis Association">Women's Tennis Association</a> as they were ranked the number one female tennis player.
</p><p>
The <a href="/wiki/Spa-Francorchamps" class="mw-redirect" title="Spa-Francorchamps">Spa-Francorchamps</a> motor-racing circuit hosts the <a href="/wiki/Formula_One_World_Championship" class="mw-redirect" title="Formula One World Championship">Formula One World Championship</a> <a href="/wiki/Belgian_Grand_Prix" title="Belgian Grand Prix">Belgian Grand Prix</a>. The Belgian driver, <a href="/wiki/Jacky_Ickx" title="Jacky Ickx">Jacky Ickx</a>, won eight Grands Prix and six <a href="/wiki/24_Hours_of_Le_Mans" title="24 Hours of Le Mans">24 Hours of Le Mans</a> and finished twice as runner-up in the Formula One World Championship. Belgium also has a strong reputation in, <a href="/wiki/Motocross" title="Motocross">motocross</a> with the rider <a href="/wiki/Stefan_Everts" title="Stefan Everts">Stefan Everts</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-215" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-215">&#91;206&#93;</a></sup> Sporting events annually held in Belgium include the <a href="/wiki/Memorial_Van_Damme" title="Memorial Van Damme">Memorial Van Damme</a> athletics competition, the <a href="/wiki/Belgian_Grand_Prix" title="Belgian Grand Prix">Belgian Grand Prix</a> Formula One, and a number of <a href="/wiki/Classic_cycle_races" title="Classic cycle races">classic cycle races</a> such as the <a href="/wiki/Tour_of_Flanders" title="Tour of Flanders">Tour of Flanders</a> and <a href="/wiki/Li%C3%A8ge%E2%80%93Bastogne%E2%80%93Li%C3%A8ge" title="Liège–Bastogne–Liège">Liège–Bastogne–Liège</a>. The <a href="/wiki/1920_Summer_Olympics" title="1920 Summer Olympics">1920 Summer Olympics</a> were held in Antwerp. The <a href="/wiki/1977_European_Basketball_Championship" class="mw-redirect" title="1977 European Basketball Championship">1977 European Basketball Championship</a> was held in <a href="/wiki/Li%C3%A8ge" title="Liège">Liège</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ostend" title="Ostend">Ostend</a>.</p><div style="clear:both;"></div>

<li id="cite_note-81"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-81">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The Constitution set out seven institutions each of which can have a parliament, government and administration. In fact, there are only six such bodies because the Flemish Region merged into the Flemish Community. This single Flemish body thus exercises powers about Community matters in the bilingual area of Brussels-Capital and in the Dutch language area, while about Regional matters only in Flanders.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-97"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-97">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The richest (per capita income) of Belgium's three regions is the <a href="/wiki/Flemish_Region" title="Flemish Region">Flemish Region</a>, followed by the <a href="/wiki/Walloon_Region" class="mw-redirect" title="Walloon Region">Walloon Region</a> and lastly the <a href="/wiki/Brussels-Capital_Region" class="mw-redirect" title="Brussels-Capital Region">Brussels-Capital Region</a>. The ten municipalities with the highest reported income are: <a href="/wiki/Laethem-Saint-Martin" class="mw-redirect" title="Laethem-Saint-Martin">Laethem-Saint-Martin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Keerbergen" title="Keerbergen">Keerbergen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lasne" title="Lasne">Lasne</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oud-Heverlee" title="Oud-Heverlee">Oud-Heverlee</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hove,_Belgium" title="Hove, Belgium">Hove</a>, <a href="/wiki/De_Pinte" title="De Pinte">De Pinte</a>, <a href="/wiki/Meise" title="Meise">Meise</a>, <a href="/wiki/Knokke-Heist" title="Knokke-Heist">Knokke-Heist</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bierbeek" title="Bierbeek">Bierbeek</a>.<cite class="citation web"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20110827090211/http://trends.rnews.be/fr/economie/actualite/politique-economique/ou-habitent-les-belges-les-plus-riches/article-1194966031033.htm">"Où habitent les Belges les plus riches?"</a>. trends.be. 2010. Archived from <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://trends.rnews.be/fr/economie/actualite/politique-economique/ou-habitent-les-belges-les-plus-riches/article-1194966031033.htm">the original</a> on 27 August 2011<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">15 July</span> 2011</span>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.btitle=O%C3%B9+habitent+les+Belges+les+plus+riches%3F&amp;rft.pub=trends.be&amp;rft.date=2010&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Ftrends.rnews.be%2Ffr%2Feconomie%2Factualite%2Fpolitique-economique%2Fou-habitent-les-belges-les-plus-riches%2Farticle-1194966031033.htm&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ABelgium" </li>
<li id="cite_note-143"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-143">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Native speakers of Dutch living in Wallonia and of French in Flanders are relatively small minorities that furthermore largely balance one another, hence attributing all inhabitants of each unilingual area to the area's language can cause only insignificant inaccuracies (99% can speak the language). Dutch: Flanders' 6.079&#160;million inhabitants and about 15% of Brussels' 1.019&#160;million are 6.23&#160;million or 59.3% of the 10.511&#160;million inhabitants of Belgium (2006); German: 70,400 in the German-speaking Community (which has <a href="/wiki/Municipalities_with_language_facilities" title="Municipalities with language facilities">language facilities</a> for its less than 5% French-speakers) and an estimated 20,000–25,000 speakers of German in the Walloon Region outside the geographical boundaries of their official Community, or 0.9%; French: in the latter area as well as mainly in the rest of Wallonia (3.321&#160;million) and 85% of the Brussels inhabitants (0.866&#160;million) thus 4.187&#160;million or 39.8%; together indeed 100%.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-144"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-144">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Flemish Academic Eric Corijn (initiator of <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.charta91.be/">Charta 91</a>), at a colloquium regarding Brussels, on 2001-12-05, states that in Brussels 91% of the population speaks French at home, either alone or with another language, and about 20% speaks Dutch at home, either alone (9%) or with French (11%)—After ponderation, the repartition can be estimated at between 85 and 90% French-speaking, and the remaining are Dutch-speaking, corresponding to the estimations based on languages chosen in Brussels by citizens for their official documents (ID, driving licenses, weddings, birth, sex, and so on); all these statistics on language are also available at Belgian Department of Justice (for weddings, birth, sex), Department of Transport (for Driving licenses), Department of Interior (for IDs), because there are no means to know <i>precisely</i> the proportions since Belgium has abolished 'official' linguistic censuses, thus official documents on language choices can only be estimations. For a web source on this topic, see e.g. <a href="#General_online_sources">General online sources: Janssens, Rudi</a></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-191"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-191">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Notable Belgian films based on works by Flemish authors include: <i>De Witte</i> (author <a href="/wiki/Ernest_Claes" title="Ernest Claes">Ernest Claes</a>) movie by Jan Vanderheyden and Edith Kiel in 1934, remake as <i>De Witte van Sichem</i> directed by <a href="/wiki/Robbe_De_Hert" title="Robbe De Hert">Robbe De Hert</a> in 1980; <i>De man die zijn haar kort liet knippen</i> (<a href="/wiki/Johan_Daisne" title="Johan Daisne">Johan Daisne</a>) <a href="/wiki/Andr%C3%A9_Delvaux" title="André Delvaux">André Delvaux</a> 1965; <i>Mira</i> ('De teleurgang van de Waterhoek' by <a href="/wiki/Stijn_Streuvels" title="Stijn Streuvels">Stijn Streuvels</a>) <a href="/wiki/Fons_Rademakers" title="Fons Rademakers">Fons Rademakers</a> 1971; <i><a href="/wiki/Malpertuis" title="Malpertuis">Malpertuis</a> (aka The Legend of Doom House)</i> (<a href="/wiki/Jean_Ray_(author)" title="Jean Ray (author)">Jean Ray</a> [pen name of Flemish author who mainly wrote in French, or as John Flanders in Dutch]) <a href="/wiki/Harry_K%C3%BCmel" title="Harry Kümel">Harry Kümel</a> 1971; <i>De loteling</i> (<a href="/wiki/Hendrik_Conscience" title="Hendrik Conscience">Hendrik Conscience</a>) Roland Verhavert 1974; <i>Dood van een non</i> (<a href="/wiki/Maria_Rosseels" title="Maria Rosseels">Maria Rosseels</a>) Paul Collet and Pierre Drouot 1975; <i>Pallieter</i> (<a href="/wiki/Felix_Timmermans" title="Felix Timmermans">Felix Timmermans</a>) Roland Verhavert 1976; <i>De komst van Joachim Stiller</i> (<a href="/wiki/Hubert_Lampo" title="Hubert Lampo">Hubert Lampo</a>) <a href="/wiki/Harry_K%C3%BCmel" title="Harry Kümel">Harry Kümel</a> 1976; <i><a href="/wiki/De_Leeuw_van_Vlaanderen_(novel)" class="mw-redirect" title="De Leeuw van Vlaanderen (novel)">De Leeuw van Vlaanderen</a></i> (<a href="/wiki/Hendrik_Conscience" title="Hendrik Conscience">Hendrik Conscience</a>) <a href="/wiki/Hugo_Claus" title="Hugo Claus">Hugo Claus</a> (a famous author himself) 1985; <i><a href="/wiki/Daens_(film)" title="Daens (film)">Daens</a></i> ('Pieter Daens' by <a href="/wiki/Louis_Paul_Boon" title="Louis Paul Boon">Louis Paul Boon</a>) <a href="/wiki/Stijn_Coninx" title="Stijn Coninx">Stijn Coninx</a> 1992; see also <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20070514023803/http://www.ledoux.be/nl/dvdmain.htm">Filmarchief <i>les DVD!s de la cinémathèque</i></a> (in Dutch). Retrieved on <span class="nowrap">7 June</span> 2007.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-194"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-194">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The Dutch word 'ommegang' is here used in the sense of an entirely or mainly non-religious procession, or the non-religious part thereof—see also <a href="https://nl.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ommegang" class="extiw" title="nl:Ommegang">its article on the Dutch-language Wikipedia</a>; the Processional Giants of Brussels, Dendermonde and Mechelen mentioned in this paragraph are part of each city's 'ommegang'. The French word 'ducasse' refers also to a procession; the mentioned Processional Giants of Ath and Mons are part of each city's 'ducasse'.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-201"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-201">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Contrarily to what the text suggests, the season starts as early as July and lasts through April.</span>
</li>

<li id="cite_note-73"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-73">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation book">Kramer, Johannes (1984). <i>Zweisprachigkeit in den Benelux-ländern</i> (in German). Buske Verlag. p.&#160;69. <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-3-87118-597-7" title="Special:BookSources/978-3-87118-597-7"><bdi>978-3-87118-597-7</bdi></a>. <q>Zur prestige Sprache wurde in den Spanischen Niederlanden ganz eindeutig das Französische. Die Vertreter Spaniens beherrschten normalerweise das Französische, nicht aber das Niederländische; ein beachtlicher Teil der am Hofe tätigen Adligen stammte aus Wallonien, das sich ja eher auf die spanische Seite geschlagen hatte als Flandern und Brabant. In dieser Situation war es selbstverständlich, dass die flämischen Adligen, die im Laufe der Zeit immer mehr ebenfalls zu Hofbeamten wurden, sich des Französischen bedienen mussten, wenn sie als gleichwertig anerkannt werden wollten. [Transl.: The prestigious language in the Spanish Netherlands was clearly French. Spain's representatives usually mastered French but not Dutch; a notable part of the nobles at the court came from Wallonia, which had taken party for the Spanish side to a higher extent than Flanders and Brabant. It was therefore evident within this context that the Flemish nobility, of which a progressively larger number became servants of the court, had to use French, if it wanted to get acknowledged as well.]</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Zweisprachigkeit+in+den+Benelux-l%C3%A4ndern&amp;rft.pages=69&amp;rft.pub=Buske+Verlag&amp;rft.date=1984&amp;rft.isbn=978-3-87118-597-7&amp;rft.au=Kramer%2C+Johannes&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ABelgium" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886058088"/></span>

<li id="cite_note-83"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-83">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation book">Lagasse, Charles-Etienne (2003). <i>Les nouvelles institutions politiques de la Belgique et de l'Europe</i>. Namur: Erasme. p.&#160;289. <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-2-87127-783-5" title="Special:BookSources/978-2-87127-783-5"><bdi>978-2-87127-783-5</bdi></a>. <q>In 2002, 58.92% of the fiscal income was going to the budget of the federal government, but more than one-third was used to pay the interests of the public debt. Without including this post, the share of the federal government budget would be only 48.40% of the fiscal income. There are 87.8% of the civil servants who are working for the Regions or the Communities and 12.2% for the Federal State.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Les+nouvelles+institutions+politiques+de+la+Belgique+et+de+l%27Europe&amp;rft.place=Namur&amp;rft.pages=289&amp;rft.pub=Erasme&amp;rft.date=2003&amp;rft.isbn=978-2-87127-783-5&amp;rft.au=Lagasse%2C+Charles-Etienne&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ABelgium" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886058088"/></span>

<li id="cite_note-Suinen-88"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Suinen_88-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web">Suinen, Philippe (October 2000). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.monde-diplomatique.fr/2000/10/SUINEN/14406.html">"Une Première mondiale"</a>. <i><a href="/wiki/Le_Monde_diplomatique" title="Le Monde diplomatique">Le Monde diplomatique</a></i> (in French). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20001117170500/http://www.monde-diplomatique.fr/2000/10/SUINEN/14406.html">Archived</a> from the original on 17 November 2000<span class="reference-accessdate">. <li id="cite_note-116"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-116">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://plantaardigheden.nl/dodoens/over_dodoens/leven_en_werk.htm#dodoens">"Rembert Dodoens: iets over zijn leven en werk—Dodoens' werken"</a>. <i>Plantaardigheden—Project Rembert Dodoens (Rembertus Dodonaeus)</i> (in Dutch). Balkbrug: Stichting Kruidenhoeve/Plantaardigheden. 20 December 2005. <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20070610070835/http://www.plantaardigheden.nl/dodoens/over_dodoens/leven_en_werk.htm">Archived</a> from the original on 10 June 2007<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">17 May</span> 2007</span>. <q>&#160;het Cruijdeboeck, dat in 1554 verscheen. Dit meesterwerk was na de bijbel in die tijd het meest vertaalde boek. Het werd gedurende meer dan een eeuw steeds weer heruitgegeven en gedurende meer dan twee eeuwen was het het meest gebruikte handboek over kruiden in West-Europa. Het is een werk van wereldfaam en grote wetenschappelijke waarde. De nieuwe gedachten die Dodoens erin neerlegde, werden de bouwstenen voor de botanici en medici van latere generaties. <i>(...&#160;the Cruijdeboeck, published in 1554. This masterpiece was, after the Bible, the most translated book in that time. It continued to be republished for more than a century and for more than two centuries it was the mostly used referential about herbs. It is a work with world fame and great scientific value. The new thoughts written down by Dodoens, became the building bricks for botanists and physicians of later generations.)</i></q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.jtitle=Plantaardigheden%E2%80%94Project+Rembert+Dodoens+%28Rembertus+Dodonaeus%29&amp;rft.atitle=Rembert+Dodoens%3A+iets+over+zijn+leven+en+werk%E2%80%94Dodoens%27+werken&amp;rft.date=2005-12-20&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fplantaardigheden.nl%2Fdodoens%2Fover_dodoens%2Fleven_en_werk.htm%23dodoens&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ABelgium" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886058088"/></span>

(2004). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20070609192011/http://www-groups.dcs.st-andrews.ac.uk/~history/Biographies/Stevin.html">"Simon Stevin"</a>. School of Mathematics and Statistics, University of St Andrews, Scotland. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">11 May</span> 2007</span>. <q>Although he did not invent decimals (they had been used by the Arabs and the Chinese long before Stevin's time) he did introduce their use in mathematics in Europe.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.btitle=Simon+Stevin&amp;rft.pub=School+of+Mathematics+and+Statistics%2C+University+of+St+Andrews%2C+Scotland&amp;rft.date=2004&amp;rft.aulast=O%27Connor&amp;rft.aufirst=J.+J.&amp;rft.au=Robertsonfirst2%3DE.+F.&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww-groups.dcs.st-andrews.ac.uk%2F~history%2FBiographies%2FStevin.html&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ABelgium" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886058088"/></span>
